A.|location=Lisbon}}</ref>}} [[Exclusive economic zone of Portugal|Portugal's exclusive economic zone]] extends over {{Convert|1,727,408|km2|mi2|abbr=on}}, making it the third-largest in the European Union and the twentieth-largest in the world.<ref name="dgrm.pt" /> The country's highest point is the summit of [[Mount Pico]], located on [[Pico Island]] in the Azores, which rises to an elevation of {{convert|2351|m|ft|abbr=on}} above sea level.<ref>{{cite web|publication-place=Amadora|publisher=Laboratório Nacional de Energia e Geologia, I.P.|title=Pico Island, scale 1:50 000|website=geoPortal do LNEG|url=https://geoportal.lneg.pt/en/opendata/geological_maps/geologic_maps_azores/picoisland/|author=Geological Services of Portugal|year=1962|access-date=22 February 2026}}</ref>{{efn|The highest peak in [[Continental Portugal|mainland Portugal]] is [[Torre (Serra da Estrela)|Torre]] in [[Serra da Estrela]], at an elevation of {{convert|1993|m|ft}}.<ref>{{cite web|title=Simplified Geological Map of Serra da Estrela Natural Park, scale 1:75 000|website=geoPortal do LNEG|url=https://geoportal.lneg.pt/en/opendata/geological_maps/diverse_maps/serraestrelanaturalparkmap_75k/|author=Instituto Geológico e Mineiro and Instituto de Conservação da Natureza|year=1999|publication-place=Amadora|access-date=22 February 2026|publisher=Laboratório Nacional de Energia e Geologia, I.P.}}</ref>}} Despite the country's size, Portugal exhibits a diverse array of [[geomorphological]] landscapes as a result of its long geological evolution, shaped by two [[Wilson Cycle|Wilson cycles]], its position relative to [[Plate tectonics|plate boundaries]], and climatic variability that produced distinct [[morphoclimatic zones]].<ref>{{cite book|editor-last1=Vieira|editor-first1=Gonçalo|editor-last2=Luís|editor-first2=Zêzere José|editor-last3=Mora|editor-first3=Carla|first1=Catarina|last1=Ramos|first2=Ana|last2=Ramos-Pereira|chapter=Chapter 1: Landscapes of Portugal: Paleogeographic Evolution, Tectonics and Geomorphology|title=Landscapes and Landforms of Portugal|publication-date=23 May 2020|publisher= Springer Nature Switzerland AG|isbn=978-3-319-03640-3|series= World Geomorphological Landscapes |page=28|issn= 2213-2090|eissn=2213-2104|publication-place=Cham|doi=10.1007/978-3-319-03641-0_1|oclc=1156020287}}</ref>

Continental Portugal is 67% forests and 24% agricultural. The Portuguese mainland is predominantly low-altitude, with over 70% of the territory lying below {{convert|400|m|ft|abbr=on}} and less than 12% rising above {{convert|700|m|ft|abbr=on}} of elevation. Its geography is structured by the [[Tagus]] River, which enters from Spain and flows into the [[Tagus Estuary Natural Reserve|Tagus Estuary]], as 95% of areas exceeding {{convert|400|m|ft|abbr=on}} are situated to the north of the river while the regions south of the Tagus, encompassing [[Alentejo]] and the [[Algarve]], have 62% of the lands below {{convert|200|m|ft|abbr=on}}. The territory north of the Tagus is marked by mountains and plateaus incised by river valleys, whereas the south is distinguished by rolling plains.<ref name="areaAgriculture">{{cite web|author=Institute for Nature Conservation and Forests |date= January 2021|title= Portugal Perfil Florestal|publication-place= Lisbon |publisher= self-published|url=https://www.icnf.pt/api/file/doc/1f924a3c0e4f7372|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20250902133502/https://www.icnf.pt/api/file/doc/1f924a3c0e4f7372|archive-date=2 September 2025|access-date=21 April 2026|trans-title=Portugal: Forest Profile|language=pt-PT|page=1}}</ref><ref>{{cite book|editor-last1=Vieira|editor-first1=Gonçalo|editor-last2=Luís|editor-first2=Zêzere José|editor-last3=Mora|editor-first3=Carla|first1=Catarina|last1=Ramos|first2=Ana|last2=Ramos-Pereira|chapter=Chapter 1: Landscapes of Portugal: Paleogeographic Evolution, Tectonics and Geomorphology|title=Landscapes and Landforms of Portugal|publication-date=23 May 2020|publisher= Springer Nature Switzerland AG|isbn=978-3-319-03640-3|series= World Geomorphological Landscapes |pages=13–25|issn= 2213-2090|eissn=2213-2104|publication-place=Cham|doi=10.1007/978-3-319-03641-0_1|oclc=1156020287}}</ref>

The Madeira archipelago comprises the islands of [[Madeira Island|Madeira]] and [[Porto Santo]], together with the [[Desertas Islands|Desertas]] and [[Savage Islands]], all of which are of volcanic origin. Approximately one third of Madeira Island lies above {{convert|1000|m|ft}} in elevation, and its landscape is characterised by a dense network of deep valleys with slopes rising several hundred metres, as well as streams that originate in the island's centre and diverge towards the coast, sustained by abundant rainfall. The steep gradient and very high rainfall is a cause of [[flash floods]] with high [[sediment transport]].<ref>{{cite book|editor-last1=Vieira|editor-first1=Gonçalo|editor-last2=Luís|editor-first2=Zêzere José|editor-last3=Mora|editor-first3=Carla|first1=Catarina|last1=Ramos|first2=Ana|last2=Ramos-Pereira|chapter=Chapter 1: Landscapes of Portugal: Paleogeographic Evolution, Tectonics and Geomorphology|title=Landscapes and Landforms of Portugal|publication-date=23 May 2020|publisher= Springer Nature Switzerland AG|isbn=978-3-319-03640-3|series= World Geomorphological Landscapes |pages=25–26|issn= 2213-2090|eissn=2213-2104|publication-place=Cham|doi=10.1007/978-3-319-03641-0_1|oclc=1156020287}}</ref>

The Azores is an archipelago composed of nine volcanic islands which, from west to east, are [[Flores Island (Azores)|Flores]], [[Corvo Island|Corvo]], [[Faial Island|Faial]], [[Pico Island|Pico]], [[São Jorge Island|São Jorge]], [[Graciosa Island|Graciosa]], [[Terceira Island|Terceira]], [[São Miguel Island|São Miguel]], and [[Santa Maria Island|Santa Maria]]. The islands retain much of their volcanic landforms, most visibly in volcanic cones and in the lakes that shape the scenery of the islands especially São Miguel, Flores, Terceira, Pico, and Corvo. Although rainfall is abundant, most streams in the Azores are temporary, and the predominance of agricultural land use further accentuates the torrential nature of the river regime during periods of intense precipitation.<ref>{{cite book|editor-last1=Vieira|editor-first1=Gonçalo|editor-last2=Luís|editor-first2=Zêzere José|editor-last3=Mora|editor-first3=Carla|first1=Catarina|last1=Ramos|first2=Ana|last2=Ramos-Pereira|chapter=Chapter 1: Landscapes of Portugal: Paleogeographic Evolution, Tectonics and Geomorphology|title=Landscapes and Landforms of Portugal|publication-date=23 May 2020|publisher= Springer Nature Switzerland AG|isbn=978-3-319-03640-3|series= World Geomorphological Landscapes |pages=26–28|issn= 2213-2090|eissn=2213-2104|publication-place=Cham|doi=10.1007/978-3-319-03641-0_1|oclc=1156020287}}</ref><ref name="areaAgriculture" />

=== Climate ===
{{Main|Climate of Portugal|Climate change in Portugal}}

{{Image frame|align=right|border=yes|caption=The [[Köppen climate classification|Köppen climate types]] of Portugal|content=

The climate of Portugal is mainly [[Mediterranean climate|Mediterranean]]. While the mainland and Madeira show a Mediterranean climate, the Azores mainly have a [[Oceanic climate|temperate oceanic climate]]. Portugal has a diverse variety of regional climates for a country of its size.<ref name="Mora Vieira The Climate of Portugal">{{cite book|editor-last1=Vieira|editor-first1=Gonçalo|editor-last2=Luís|editor-first2=Zêzere José|editor-last3=Mora|editor-first3=Carla|first1=Carla|last1=Mora|first2=Gonçalo|last2=Vieira|chapter=Chapter 2: The Climate of Portugal|title=Landscapes and Landforms of Portugal|publication-date=23 May 2020|publisher= Springer Nature Switzerland AG|isbn=978-3-319-03640-3|series= World Geomorphological Landscapes |pages=33–46|issn= 2213-2090|eissn=2213-2104|publication-place=Cham|doi=10.1007/978-3-319-03641-0_2|oclc=1156020287}}</ref>

The Iberian Peninsula is located at the southern margin of the temperate zone and at the northern margin of the subtropical [[High-pressure area|high-pressure zone]]. Additionally, Portugal's climate is influenced by the seasonal latitudinal shift of the [[jet stream]], which directly impacts the trajectory of a [[polar front]]. Typically in the winter, the jet stream moves southwards and Portugal comes under the influence of the polar front, producing colder temperatures. When the polar front moves northward, Portugal comes under the influence of the stable atmospheric conditions that bring milder weather during the summer.<ref name="Mora Vieira The Climate of Portugal"/>

The high altitude zones of the Azorean islands have a [[Oceanic climate|temperate maritime climate]] while the western Azores have a [[humid subtropical climate]]. In parts of the [[Beja District]] and on [[Porto Santo Island]] the climate is [[semi-arid climate|semi-arid]]. In the [[Savage Islands|Selvagens Islands]] the climate is that of a [[hot desert climate|hot desert]]. Portugal is one of the warmest countries in Europe: the average temperature in [[mainland Portugal]] varies from {{convert|10-12|°C|°F|1}} in the mountainous interior north to {{convert|17-19|°C|°F|1}} in the south and on the [[Guadiana]] [[river basin]], with variations from the highlands to the lowlands.<ref>{{cite journal |last1=Beck |first1=Hylke E. |last2=McVicar |first2=Tim R. |last3=Vergopolan |first3=Noemi |last4=Berg |first4=Alexis |last5=Lutsko |first5=Nicholas J. |last6=Dufour |first6=Ambroise |last7=Zeng |first7=Zhenzhong |last8=Jiang |first8=Xin |last9=van Dijk |first9=Albert I. J. M. |last10=Miralles |first10=Diego G. |title=High-resolution (1 km) Köppen-Geiger maps for 1901–2099 based on constrained CMIP6 projections |journal=Scientific Data |date=23 October 2023 |volume=10 |issue=1 |article-number=724 |doi=10.1038/s41597-023-02549-6 |pmid=37872197 |doi-access=free |pmc=10593765 |bibcode=2023NatSD..10..724B }}</ref>

[[Wildfire]]s remain a serious challenge in Portugal, where 99% of the cases reported by law enforcement in 2024 were of unknown origin.{{sfn|Forest fires in Europe|2025|p=102}} Between 2014 and 2024, Portugal recorded an annual average of 12,496 fires and {{convert|112455|ha|sqmi|0|abbr=on}} burned, making it the European Union country with both the highest average number of wildfires and the greatest average burned area over that period.{{sfn|Forest fires in Europe|2025|p=13}} [[Climate change in Portugal|Climate change]] is projected to raise average temperatures in Portugal by as much as {{convert|4|°C|°F|1}} by 2100 relative to the 1970–2010 average, with likely consequences for the country's energy supply, particularly by diminishing electricity generation capacity.<ref>{{multiref2
|1={{cite report|pages=122–126|url=https://unfccc.int/files/national_reports/annex_i_natcom_/application/pdf/28410365_portugal-nc7-1-pt7cn3brfinal.pdf|title=7th National Communication to the United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change, 3rd Biennial Report to the United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change, 4th National Communication in the Context of the Kyoto Protocol|author=Portuguese Environment Agency - Climate Change Department|access-date=28 April 2026|publication-date=December 2017|publication-place=Amadora|publisher=Portuguese Environment Agency}}
|2={{cite report|page=31|title=Relatório do Subgrupo Energia para uma Estratégia Nacional de Adaptação às Alterações Climáticas: Medidas e Ações de Adaptação do Setor Energético|url=https://apambiente.pt/sites/default/files/_Clima/Adapta%C3%A7%C3%A3o/Relat_Setor_ENAAC_Energia.pdf|publication-date=December 2012|publisher= Agência Portuguesa do Ambiente, I. P.|publication-place=Lisbon|author=Energy Subgroup for the National Strategy for Adaptation to Climate Change|trans-title=Report of the Energy Subgroup for a National Strategy for Adaptation to Climate Change: Adaptation Measures and Actions for the Energy Sector|language=pt-PT|access-date=28 April 2026}}}}</ref>

=== Biodiversity ===
{{Main|Biodiversity of Portugal}}

[[File:Miradouro da Cascata do Arado.jpg|right|thumb|The [[Peneda-Gerês National Park]] in [[North Region, Portugal|Northern Portugal]] is the only national park in Portugal.<ref>{{cite act |author=Office of the Secretary of State for Spatial Planning and Nature Conservation |trans-title=Order No. 3578/2017 |at=No. 82/2017, Series 2|location={{lang|pt-PT|[[Diário da República]]}} |url=https://diariodarepublica.pt/dr/detalhe/despacho/3578-2017-106927067|access-date=28 April 2026|date=27 April 2017|language=pt-PT|title=Despacho n.º 3578/2017}}</ref>|alt=A wide view of a forested mountain valley in the Peneda-Gerês National Park under grey clouds, with rocky slopes on both sides, a stream running through the centre, and a small stone bridge partly hidden among the trees]]

Portugal is located on the [[Mediterranean basin]], the 3rd most diverse hotspot of flora in the world.<ref>{{cite book|title=Hotspots revisited: earth's biologically richest and most endangered terrestrial ecoregions|publisher=Cemex|publication-place=Mexico City|publication-date=December 2004|first=Russell A. |last=Mittermeier|display-authors=etal|page=33|volume=392|isbn=968-6397-77-9|oclc=1409005657}}</ref> It is home to 6 terrestrial ecoregions - [[Azores temperate mixed forests]], [[Cantabrian mixed forests]], [[Madeira evergreen forests]], [[Iberian sclerophyllous and semi-deciduous forests]], [[Northwest Iberian montane forests]], and [[Southwest Iberian Mediterranean sclerophyllous and mixed forests]].<ref name="DinersteinOlson2017">{{cite journal |last1=Dinerstein |first1=Eric |last2=Olson |first2=David |last3=Joshi |first3=Anup |last4=Vynne |first4=Carly |last5=Burgess |first5=Neil D. |last6=Wikramanayake |first6=Eric |last7=Hahn |first7=Nathan |last8=Palminteri |first8=Suzanne |last9=Hedao |first9=Prashant |last10=Noss |first10=Reed |last11=Hansen |first11=Matt |last12=Locke |first12=Harvey |last13=Ellis |first13=Erle C |last14=Jones |first14=Benjamin |last15=Barber |first15=Charles Victor |last16=Hayes |first16=Randy |last17=Kormos |first17=Cyril |last18=Martin |first18=Vance |last19=Crist |first19=Eileen |last20=Sechrest |first20=Wes |last21=Price |first21=Lori |last22=Baillie |first22=Jonathan E. M. |last23=Weeden |first23=Don |last24=Suckling |first24=Kierán |last25=Davis |first25=Crystal |last26=Sizer |first26=Nigel |last27=Moore |first27=Rebecca |last28=Thau |first28=David |last29=Birch |first29=Tanya |last30=Potapov |first30=Peter |last31=Turubanova |first31=Svetlana |last32=Tyukavina |first32=Alexandra |last33=de Souza |first33=Nadia |last34=Pintea |first34=Lilian |last35=Brito |last41=Klöser |first41=Heinz |last42=Shennan-Farpón |first42=Yara |last43=Kindt |first43=Roeland |last44=Lillesø |first44=Jens-Peter Barnekow |last45=van Breugel |first45=Paulo |last46=Graudal June 2017|url-status=live}}</ref> Over 22% of its land area is included in the [[Natura 2000]] network.<ref name="dre">{{cite act |author=Office of the Secretary of State for Spatial Planning and of continental Portugal.<ref>{{cite report|title=Inventário Florestal Nacional|edition=6th|page=3|url=https://www.icnf.pt/api/file/doc/0f0165f9df0d0bbe|year=2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230507142758/https://www.icnf.pt/api/file/doc/0f0165f9df0d0bbe|archive-date=7 Faias|publication-place=Lisbon|publication-date=28 June 2019|trans-title=National Forest Inventory|language=pt-PT}}</ref>
The Portuguese west coast is part of the four major Eastern Boundary [[Upwelling]] Systems of the ocean.<ref>{{cite web |last1=Correia |first1=Paulo Filipe Alexandre |title=Study of an upwelling event in the Portuguese coast |url=https://fenix.tecnico.ulisboa.pt/downloadFile/563345090415834/Tese_Paulo%20Correia_final.pdf |access-date=22 March 2021 |archive-date=14 April 2021 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210414133259/https://fenix.tecnico.ulisboa.pt/downloadFile/563345090415834/Tese_Paulo%20Correia_final.pdf |url-status=live }}</ref> 73% of the [[freshwater fish]] occurring in the [[Iberian Peninsula]] are endemic, the largest out of any region in Europe.<ref>{{cite journal |last1=Rodeles |first1=Amaia A. |last2=Galicia |first2=David |last3=Miranda |first3=Rafael |title=Iberian fish records in the vertebrate collection of the Museum of Zoology of the University of Navarra |journal=Scientific Data |date=11 October 2016 |volume=3 |issue=1 |article-number=160091 |doi=10.1038/sdata.2016.91 |pmid=27727236 |pmc=5058334 |bibcode=2016NatSD...360091R }}</ref> Among Portugal's [[protected areas of Portugal|protected areas]] are the [[Southwest Alentejo and Vicentine Coast Natural Park]], one of Europe's last remaining stretches of wild coastline, and [[Montesinho Natural Park]], which preserves one of the few thriving [[Northwest Iberian montane forests|Mediterranean mountain landscapes]] and is an example of successful coexistence between human communities and nature.<ref>{{multiref2
|1={{cite journal |last1=Bastos |first1=Maria Rosário |last2=Dias |first2=João A. |last3=Baptista |first3=Manuela |last4=Batista |first4=Carla |title=Ocupação do Litoral do Alentejo, Portugal: passado e presente |journal=Revista de Gestão Costeira Integrada / Journal of Integrated Coastal Zone Management|publisher=Associação Portuguesa dos Recursos Hídricos|publication-place=Lisbon|date=March 2012 |volume=12|language=pt-PT|trans-title=Occupation of the Alentejo Coast, Portugal: past and present|issue=1 |pages=99–116 |doi=10.5894/rgci307 |issn=1646-8872|doi-access=free }}
|2={{cite book|pages=151–154|doi=10.1007/978-3-642-01577-9_18|publication-date=24 August 2009|isbn=978-3-642-01577-9|chapter=Land Use, Landscape and Sustainability: Examples from Montesinho|title=Natural heritage from east to west: case studies from 6 EU countries|first=José|last=Castro|editor-first1=Niki|editor-last1=Evelpidou|editor-first2=Tomás |editor-last2=Figueiredo|editor-first3=Francesco |editor-last3=Mauro|editor-first4=Vahap|editor-last4=Tecim|editor-first5=Andreas|edition=1st |editor-last5=Vassilopoulos|lccn= 2009932879|publisher=Springer-Verlag Berlin Heidelberg|oclc=574719991|publication-place=Berlin |hdl=10198/7252 }}}}</ref>

Geographical and climatic conditions facilitate the introduction of exotic species that later turn out to be invasive and destructive to the native habitats. Around 20% of the total number of extant species in continental Portugal are [[Introduced species|exotic]].<ref>{{cite journal |last1=de Almeida |first1=João Domingues |title=New additions to the exotic vascular flora of continental Portugal |journal=Flora Mediterranea |publication-date= 20 December 2018 |pages=259–278| publisher=Fondazione Internazionale Pro Herbario Mediterraneo|publication-place=Palermo, Sicily|issn=2240-4538|volume=28 |doi=10.7320/FlMedit28.259 |doi-access=free|url=https://herbmedit.org/storage/1278/FL28_259-278.pdf|access-date=22 April 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260322020720/https://herbmedit.org/storage/1278/FL28_259-278.pdf|archive-date=22 March 2026|url-status=live}}</ref> Portugal is the 2nd country in Europe with the highest number of threatened animal and plant species.<ref>{{cite web |author=IUCN|publisher=self-published|title=IUCN Red List of Threatened Species|version=2025-2|url=https://www.iucnredlist.org/statistics |website=IUCN Red List |access-date=22 April 2026|year=2025}}</ref> The country as a whole is an important stopover for migratory bird species.<ref>{{multiref2
|1={{cite journal|doi=10.1111/2041-210X.12913|doi-access=free|title=Quantifying population size of migrant birds at stopover sites: Combining count data with stopover length estimated from stable isotope analysis|volume=9|issue=3|pages=502–512|journal=Methods in Ecology and Evolution|issn=2041-210X|eissn=2041-210X|publisher=John Wiley & Sons Ltd|publication-place=Oxford|publication-date=16 October 2017|first1=Teresa|last1=Catry|first2=Pedro M.|last2=Lourenço|first3=José P.|last3=Granadeiro |bibcode=2018MEcEv...9..502C }}
|2={{cite journal|doi=10.1675/063.045.0204|publication-date=8 February 2023|pages=141–149|type=Paper|issn=1524-4695|eissn=1938-5390|publisher=The Waterbird Society|journal=Waterbirds|publication-place=Washington, D.C|volume=45|issue=2|first1=João R.|last1=Belo|first2=Maria P.|last2=Dias|first3=João|last3=Jara|first4=Amélia|last4=Almeida|first5=Frederico|last5=Morais|first6=Carlos|last6=Silva|first7=Joaquim|last7=Valadeiro|first8=José A.|last8=Alves|title=Synchronous Declines of Wintering Waders and High-Tide Roost Area in a Temperate Estuary: Results of a 10-Year Monitoring Programme}}
|3={{cite book|title=Atlas das Aves Invernantes e Migradoras de Portugal 2011-2013|page=14|hdl=10174/26177|last=Godinho|first=Carlos|date=September 2018|publication-place=Lisbon|publisher=SPEA|url=https://dspace.uevora.pt/rdpc/bitstream/10174/26177/1/Atlas_das_aves_invernantes_e_migradoras_2012_2013.pdf|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20250407100129/https://dspace.uevora.pt/rdpc/bitstream/10174/26177/1/Atlas_das_aves_invernantes_e_migradoras_2012_2013.pdf|archive-date=7 April 2025|access-date=22 April 2026|url-status=live|language=pt-PT|trans-title=Atlas of the Wintering and Migratory Birds of Portugal, 2011–2013}}}}</ref> The mammalian species of Portugal such as deer, [[Iberian ibex]], [[wild boar]], [[red fox]], [[Iberian wolf]], and [[Iberian lynx]] were once widespread throughout the country, but intense hunting, habitat degradation, and growing pressure from agriculture and livestock largely reduced their populations in the 19th and 20th centuries.<ref>{{cite book|pages=70, 72, 96, 104, 112|edition=2nd|publication-place=Évora|year=2019|isbn=978-989-8550-80-4|title= Atlas de Mamíferos de Portugal|editor-first1=Joana|editor-first2=Helena|editor-first3=Francisco|editor-first4=André E.|editor-first5=A. Márcia|editor-last1=Bencatel|editor-last2=Sabino-Marques|editor-last3= Álvares|editor-last4=Moura|editor-last5=Barbosa|url=http://atlas-mamiferos.uevora.pt/ |publisher=University of Évora |access-date=22 April 2025|language=pt-PT |archive-date=5 March 2021 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210305064847/http://atlas-mamiferos.uevora.pt/ |url-status=live|trans-title=Atlas of the Mammals of Portugal }}</ref> Others species, such as the [[Portuguese ibex]], became extinct, but some mammalian species have been re-expanding their native range.<ref>{{cite book|pages=215–231|edition=2nd|publication-place=Évora|year=2019|isbn=978-989-8550-80-4|title= Atlas de Mamíferos de Portugal|editor-first1=Joana|editor-first2=Helena|editor-first3=Francisco|editor-first4=André E.|editor-first5=A. Márcia|editor-last1=Bencatel|editor-last2=Sabino-Marques|editor-last3= Álvares|editor-last4=Moura|editor-last5=Barbosa|url=http://atlas-mamiferos.uevora.pt/ |publisher=University of Évora |access-date=22 April 2025|language=pt-PT |archive-date=5 March 2021 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210305064847/http://atlas-mamiferos.uevora.pt/ |url-status=live|trans-title=Atlas of the Mammals of Portugal }}</ref>

== Government and politics ==
{{Main|Government of Portugal|Politics of Portugal}}

{{multiple image
| alt1 = 
| alt2 = Photograph of Luís Montenegro in a dark suit, white shirt, and patterned blue tie speaking at a podium against a blue backdrop, facing forward.

| width2            = 151
| caption2          = [[Luís Montenegro]]<br /><small>[[Prime Minister of Portugal|Prime Minister]]</small>

Portugal has been a [[Semi-presidential system|semi-presidential]] representative democratic [[republic]] since the ratification of the [[Constitution of Portugal|Constitution of 1976]].<ref>{{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part IV: Guaranteeing and revision of the Constitution, Final and transitional provisions |article= 296|clause=2|quote=The Constitution of the Portuguese Republic enters into force on 25 April 1976.|edition=7th|access-date = 22 April 2026}}</ref><ref>{{cite journal |last1=Martins |first1=Ana |title=Presidential Elements in Government The Portuguese Semi-Presidential System: About Law in the Books and Law in Action |journal=European Constitutional Law Review |date=February 2006 |volume=2 |issue=1 |pages=81–100 |id={{ProQuest|216313596}} |doi=10.1017/S1574019606000812 }}</ref> The Constitution makes for a separation of powers among four [[Sovereignty body (Portugal)|sovereignty bodies]]: the [[President of Portugal|president]], the [[Government of Portugal|government]], the [[Portuguese parliament|Assembly of the Republic]], and the [[Judiciary of Portugal|courts]].<ref>{{multiref2 
|1={{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part III: Organisation of political power, Title I: General principles|article= 110|clause=1|quote=The President of the Republic, the Assembleia da República, the Government and the Courts are entities that exercise sovereignty.|edition=7th|access-date = 22 April 2026}}
|2={{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part III: Organisation of political power, Title I: General principles|article= 111|clause=1|quote=The entities that exercise sovereignty must respect the separation and interdependence laid down in the Constitution.|edition=7th|access-date = 22 April 2026}}}}</ref>

The [[head of state]] of Portugal is the [[President of Portugal|president]] who is elected to a five-year term by direct, [[universal adult suffrage]].<ref>{{multiref2 
|1={{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part III: Organisation of political power, Title II: President of the Republic, Chapter I: Status, role and election|article= 121|clause=1|quote=The President of the Republic is elected by the universal, direct and secret suffrage of Portuguesecitizens who are registered to vote in Portuguese territory and, in accordance with the following paragraph, of Portuguese citizens who reside abroad.|edition=7th|access-date = 22 April 2026}}
|2={{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part III: Organisation of political power, Title II: President of the Republic, Chapter I: Status, role and election|article= 128|clause=1|quote=The term of office of President of the Republic is five years and ends upon installation of the new President elect.|edition=7th|access-date = 22 April 2026}}}}</ref> The president exercises representative functions, holds significant governmental authority, and is able to shape media and public opinion in ways that constrain the political and policy agendas of the government and parliament; in addition, the office carries supervisory and [[reserve power]]s, includes {{lang|la|[[ex officio]]}} [[commander-in-chief|supreme command]] of the armed forces, and is advised by the [[Portuguese Council of State|Council of State]].<ref>{{multiref2
|1={{cite book|title=Direito Constitucional: diálogos em homenagem ao 80º aniversário de J. J. Gomes Canotilho|isbn= 978-65-5518-191-3|page=469|publication-place=Belo Horizonte, Minas Gerais|language=pt-BR|first1=Ana Cláudia Nascimento|last1=Gomes|first2=Bruno|last2=Albergaria|first3= Mariana Rodrigues|last3=Canotilho|publisher=Fórum|year=2021|trans-title=Constitutional Law: dialogues in tribute to the 80th birthday of J. J. Gomes Canotilho}}
|2={{cite book|title=Portugal Since the 2008 Economic Crisis|isbn=9781351046916|page=25|publication-place=London|first1=António |last1=Costa Pinto|first2=André|last2=Paris|publisher=Routledge|doi=10.4324/9781351046916-2|publication-date=11 May 2023|chapter=Chapter 2: Portuguese Democracy at 50|edition=1st}}}}</ref><ref>{{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part III: Organisation of political power, Title II: President of the Republic, Chapter II: Competences|article= 136|clause=5|quote=The President of the Republic shall also exercise the right of veto pursuant to Articles 278 and 279.|edition=7th|access-date = 28 April 2026}}</ref><ref>{{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part III: Organisation of political power, Title II: President of the Republic, Chapter I: Status, role and election|article= 120|quote=The President of the Republic represents the Portuguese Republic, guarantees national independence, the unity of the state and the proper operation of the democratic institutions, and is ex officio Commander-in-Chief of the Armed Forces.|edition=7th|access-date = 28 April 2026}}</ref><ref>{{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part III: Organisation of political power, Title II: President of the Republic, Chapter III: Council of State|article= 141|quote=The Council of State is the political organ that advises the President of the Republic.|edition=7th|access-date = 29 April 2026}}</ref> The president of Portugal is [[António José Seguro]]; he took office after winning the runoff vote of the [[2026 Portuguese presidential election]].<ref>{{cite news|first1=Andrei|last1=Khalip|first2= Sergio|last2=Goncalves|location=Lisbon |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/portugal-votes-presidential-runoff-with-socialist-poised-victory-2026-02-08/ |title=Portugal elects Socialist as president by landslide, but far right grows|publisher=Reuters |date=8 February 2026 |access-date=29 April 2026}}</ref>

Portugal's legislative body is the [[Assembly of the Republic (Portugal)|Assembly of the Republic]], an [[unicameralism|unicameral]] parliament.<ref>{{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part III: Organisation of political power, Title III: Assembleia da República, Chapter I: Status, role and election|article= 147|quote=The Assembleia da República is the assembly that represents all Portuguese citizens.|edition=7th|access-date = 22 April 2026}}</ref> It consists of a single chamber with a minimum of 180 seats and a maximum of 230, elected by popular vote every four years or when dissolved.<ref>{{multiref2
|1={{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part III: Organisation of political power, Title III: Assembleia da República, Chapter I: Status, role and election|article= 148|quote=The Assembleia da República shall have a minimum of one hundred and eighty and a maximum of two hundred and thirty Members, as laid down by electoral law.|edition=7th|access-date = 22 April 2026}}
|2={{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part III: Organisation of political power, Title III: Assembleia da República, Chapter I: Status, role and election|article= 153|clause=1|quote=Without prejudice to the suspension or termination of any individual mandate, terms of office of Members of the Assembleia da República begin with the first sitting of the Assembly following elections and end with the first sitting following the subsequent elections.|edition=7th|access-date = 22 April 2026}}
|3={{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part III: Organisation of political power, Title III: Assembleia da República, Chapter III: Organisation and modus operandi|article= 171|clause=1|quote=The duration of each legislature is four legislative sessions.|edition=7th|access-date = 22 April 2026}}
|4={{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part III: Organisation of political power, Title III: Assembleia da República, Chapter III: Organisation and modus operandi|article= 174|clause=1|quote=Legislative sessions last for one year and begin on 15 September.|edition=7th|access-date = 22 April 2026}}}}</ref> The members of parliament represent the whole country and not the constituencies for which they are elected.<ref>{{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part III: Organisation of political power, Title III: Assembleia da República, Chapter I: Status, role and election|article= 152|clause=2|quote=Members of the Assembleia da República represent the whole country and not the constituencies for which they are elected.|edition=7th|access-date = 22 April 2026}}</ref> There is [[universal suffrage]] for adults over 18 years of age, with a [[secret ballot]] for all elected offices.<ref>{{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Fundamental principles |article= 10|clause=1|quote= The people exercise political power by means of universal, equal, direct, secret and periodic suffrage, referendum and the other forms provided for in the Constitution.|edition=7th|access-date = 15 April 2026}}</ref> As the [[List of heads of government|head of government]], the [[Prime Minister of Portugal|prime minister]] leads the [[Council of Ministers (Portugal)|Council of Ministers]] which includes ministers and secretaries of state that have full executive powers,<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://diariodarepublica.pt/dr/lexionario/termo/conselho-ministros|title=Conselho de Ministros |publisher=[[Diário da República]] |access-date=7 April 2024}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://diariodarepublica.pt/dr/lexionario/termo/primeiro-ministro|title=Primeiro-Ministro |publisher=[[Diário da República]] |access-date=7 April 2024}}</ref> and is appointed by the president  in light of electoral results after consulting with the parties with seats in the Assembleia da República.<ref>{{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part III: Organisation of political power, Title IV: Government, Chapter II: Formation and accountability |article= 187|clause=1|quote=The President of the Republic appoints the Prime Minister after consulting the parties with seats in Assembleia da República and in the light of the electoral results.|edition=7th|access-date = 16 April 2026}}</ref> Portugal's prime minister is [[Luís Montenegro]] who took office after [[Democratic Alliance (Portugal, 2024)|AD – PSD/CDS Coalition]] winning enough seats to form a minority government following the [[2024 Portuguese legislative election]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.portugal.gov.pt/pt/gc24/primeiro-ministro|title=Luís Montenegro Primeiro-Ministro |date=2 April 2024 |publisher=XXIV Constitutional Government website |access-date=23 April 2024}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|first1=Catarina|last1=Demony|first2= Sergio|last2=Goncalves|location=Lisbon |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/europe/portugals-minority-government-be-sworn-stability-doubtful-2024-04-02/|title=Portugal's minority government sworn in, stability doubtful |publisher=Reuters |date=2 April 2024 |access-date=29 April 2026}}</ref> Portugal operates a multi-party system of competitive legislatures at the national, regional, and local levels. The Assembly of the Republic is dominated by three political parties, the [[Social Democratic Party (Portugal)|Social Democratic Party]] (PSD), [[Chega (political party)|Chega]] (CH), and the [[Socialist Party (Portugal)|Socialist Party]] (PS), while the PSD and PS continue to be the dominant parties in the regional parliaments and at the [[NUTS statistical regions of Portugal#LAUs|local level]].{{efn|Other parties include the [[Liberal Initiative (Portugal)|Liberal Initiative]], the [[Left Bloc (Portugal)|Left Bloc]], the [[Unitary Democratic Coalition]] ([[Portuguese Communist Party]] and [[Ecologist Party "The Greens"]]), [[LIVRE]], the [[CDS – People's Party]] and the [[People Animals Nature]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.parlamento.pt/DeputadoGP/Paginas/GruposParlamentaresI.aspx|title=Composição dos Grupos Parlamentares/Partidos |publisher=[[Assembly of the Republic (Portugal)|Assembly of the Republic]] |access-date=7 April 2024}}</ref>}} There have been recent trends towards [[Democratic backsliding|autocratisation]].<ref>{{multiref2 
|1={{cite report|chapter-url=https://www.v-dem.net/documents/75/V-Dem_Institute_Democracy_Report_2026_lowres.pdf#page=41|access-date=March 21, 2026|editor-last1=Lindberg|editor-first1=Staffan I.|first1=Nord|last1=Marina|last2=Altman|first2=David|first3=Tiago|url=https://www.v-dem.net/documents/75/V-Dem_Institute_Democracy_Report_2026_lowres.pdf|last3=Fernandes|first4=Ana Good|last4=God|publisher=[[University of Gothenburg]]: [[V-Dem Institute]]|title=Democracy Report 2026:Unraveling The Democratic Era?|edition=10th|chapter=Democracy Report 2026 Watchlist|date=March 17, 2026|quote=The eight countries that are very close to becoming autocratizers are: Bulgaria, Cyprus, Namibia, Portugal, Russia, Sierra Leone, Sudan, and Vanuatu. Three of the eight countries are new on the Watchlist this year: Bulgaria, Portugal, and Vanuatu.|quote-page=41|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260320121434/https://www.v-dem.net/documents/75/V-Dem_Institute_Democracy_Report_2026_lowres.pdf|url-status=live|archive-date=March 20, 2026}}
|2={{Cite web |title=Portugal|author= The Global State of Democracy|url=https://www.idea.int/democracytracker/country/portugal |access-date=29 April 2026 |publisher=International IDEA|date=June 2025 |quote=Between 2019 and 2024, it experienced declines in multiple factors of Representation, Rights and Rule of Law.|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260331023341/https://www.idea.int/democracytracker/country/portugal|archive-date=31 March 2026|url-status=live}}}}</ref>

Portugal has a [[Civil law (legal system)|civil law system]] based on [[Roman law]] and on [[Canon Law]] and influenced by [[Bürgerliches Gesetzbuch|German civil law]].<ref>{{cite journal|url=https://nome.unak.is/wordpress/07-1/interviews-memoirs-and-other-contributions/development-and-codification-of-private-law-in-portugal/?pdf=129|access-date=24 April 2026|title=Development and codification of private law in Portugal|last=Hamza|first=Gábor|journal=Nordicum-Mediterraneum|doi=10.33112/nm.7.1.21|year=2012|volume=7|issue=1|doi-access=free|publisher=University of Akureyri|issn=1670-6242|publication-place=Akureyri|pages=2–4|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180429133724/https://nome.unak.is/wordpress/07-1/interviews-memoirs-and-other-contributions/development-and-codification-of-private-law-in-portugal/?pdf=129|archive-date=29 April 2018|url-status=live}}</ref> The [[Constitution of Portugal|Constitution]] is the [[supreme law]] of Portugal.<ref>{{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Fundamental principles |article= 3|clause=3|quote= The validity of laws and other acts of the state, the autonomous regions, local government and any other public entities is dependent on their conformity with the Constitution.|edition=7th|access-date = 24 April 2026}}</ref> In the Portuguese legal system, [[private law|private civil law]] and [[criminal law]] are codified in the {{lang|pt-PT|[[Portuguese Civil Code|Código Civil]]}} and the {{lang|pt-PT|[[Penal Code of Portugal|Código Penal]]}} respectively.<ref>{{cite book|doi=10.4337/9781782547235.NP.4|isbn=9781782547235|publication-date=22 September 2017|oclc=966426761|title=Encyclopedia of Private International Law|publisher=Edward Elgar Publishing|chapter=Portugal|first1=Andrzej|last1=Mączyński|first2=Dário|last2=Moura Vicente|editor-first1=Jürgen|editor-last1=Basedow|editor-first2=Giesela|editor-last2=Rühl|editor-first3=Franco|editor-last3=Ferrari|editor-first4=Pedro de Miguel|editor-last4=Asensio|lccn=2016949947|publication-place=Cheltenham|page=2433}}</ref><ref>{{cite book|oclc=1335120506|doi=10.4337/9781789902990.portugal|isbn=9781789902990|publication-date=28 November 2024|title=Elgar Encyclopedia of Crime and Criminal Justice|publisher=Edward Elgar Publishing|chapter=Portugal|first1=Cristina|last1=Líbano Monteiro|editor-first1=Pedro|editor-last1=Caeiro|editor-first2=Sabine|editor-last2=Gless|editor-first3= Valsamis|editor-last3=Mitsilegas|editor-first4=Miguel João |editor-last4=Costa|editor-first5=Janneke de|editor-last5= Snaijer|editor-first6=Georgia|editor-last6=Theodorakakou|lccn=2024932274|publication-place=Cheltenham|pages=111–118}}</ref> In Portugal, courts are organised into several levels, among the judicial, administrative, and fiscal branches. The institution of last appeal is the [[Supreme Court of Justice (Portugal)|Supreme Court of Justice]]. The [[Portuguese Constitutional Court|Constitutional Court]] determines the constitutionality of the laws.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://diariodarepublica.pt/dr/lexionario/termo/tribunais|title=Tribunais |publisher=[[Diário da República]] |access-date=7 April 2024}}</ref>

=== Administrative divisions ===
{{Main|Administrative divisions of Portugal}}

Continental Portugal is agglomerated into 18 districts, while the archipelagos of the Azores and Madeira are governed as [[autonomous area|autonomous regions]]; the largest units, established since 1976, are either mainland Portugal and the [[autonomous regions of Portugal]] ([[Azores]] and [[Madeira]]).<ref>{{Cite web |title=O que são as regiões autónomas? |url=https://ffms.pt/pt-pt/direitos-e-deveres/o-que-sao-regioes-autonomas |access-date=7 December 2025 |publisher=Fundação Francisco Manuel dos Santos |language=pt}}</ref> Administratively, Portugal is divided into 308 [[municipalities of Portugal|municipalities]] (''municípios'' or {{lang|pt-PT|[[concelhos]]}}). Operationally, the municipalities, and {{lang|pt|[[freguesia]]s}}, along with the national government, are the only legally [[NUTS statistical regions of Portugal|local administrative units]] identified by the government of Portugal.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Subsetor da Administração Local - Entidades Autárquicas |url=https://portalautarquico.dgal.gov.pt/pt-PT/subsetor-da-administracao-local/entidades-autarquicas |access-date=7 December 2025 |publisher=Direção-Geral das Autarquias Locais |language=pt}}</ref> [[File:PortugalNumbered.png|right|200px|Districts of Portugal]]

Within the [[local administrative unit|European Union administrative system]] (NUTS), Portugal is divided into nine regions: the [[Azores]], [[Alentejo]], [[Algarve]], [[Centro, Portugal|Central Region]], [[Lisboa Region|Lisbon]], [[Madeira]], [[Norte, Portugal|North Region]], [[Oeste e Vale do Tejo]], and [[Península de Setúbal|Setúbal Peninsula]].<ref name="Official Journal 2023">{{Cite web |title=Official Journal L 87/2023 |url=https://eur-lex.europa.eu/legal-content/EN/TXT/HTML/?uri=OJ:L:2023:087:FULL&from=EN |access-date=13 January 2024 |website=eur-lex.europa.eu}}</ref> With the exception of the Azores and Madeira, NUTS areas are subdivided into 24 subregions.<ref>{{Cite web |title=O que são NUTS? |url=https://www.pordata.pt/pt/o-que-sao-nuts |access-date=7 December 2025 |publisher=Pordata |language=pt}}</ref>

=== Foreign relations ===
{{Main|Foreign relations of Portugal}}

[[File:Portuguese embassy map.png|thumb|[[Diplomatic missions of Portugal]]<ref>{{cite web |url=https://portaldiplomatico.mne.gov.pt/en/bilateral-relations/countries|website=Diplomatic Portal|publisher=self-published |title=Countries |author=Ministry of Foreign Affairs|author-link=Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Portugal) |access-date=6 May 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260414062402/https://portaldiplomatico.mne.gov.pt/en/bilateral-relations/countries|archive-date=14 April 2026|url-status=live}}</ref>{{resizediv|95%|{{legend|#2f3699|Countries that host a Portuguese Embassy or Consulate}}
{{legend|#b4b4b4|Countries that do not host Portuguese diplomatic missions}}
{{legend|#22b14c|Portugal}}}}|upright=1.2]]

A member state of the [[United Nations]] since 1955, Portugal is a [[International organization membership of Portugal|member of almost all major international organizations]], and is among the countries that founded [[NATO]] in 1949, the [[OECD]] in 1961, [[European Free Trade Association|EFTA]] in 1960, and the [[Community of Portuguese Language Countries]] (CPLP) in 1996, an international organisation of countries with [[Portuguese language|Portuguese]] as an official language.<ref name="ONU">{{cite journal|trans-title=Portugal and the UN: the first approach|language=pt-PT|issn=1645-9199|publisher=Instituto Português de Relações Internacionais|publication-place=Lisbon|publication-date=September 2015|journal=Relações Internacionais|issue=47|pages=9–38|url=https://ipri.unl.pt/images/publicacoes/revista_ri/pdf/ri47/n47a02.pdf|access-date=24 April 2026|title=Portugal e a ONU: a primeira aproximação|first=David|last=Castaño|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20250208131815/https://ipri.unl.pt/images/publicacoes/revista_ri/pdf/ri47/n47a02.pdf|archive-date=8 February 2025|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite book|isbn= 978-85-7631-776-0|oclc=1226359172 |title=The road ahead: the 21st-Century world order in the eyes of policy planners|publication-place=Brasília|year=2018|publisher=Fundação Alexandre de Gusmão|editor-first1=Benoni|editor-last1=Belli|editor-first2=Filipe|editor-last2=Nasser|chapter=Portuguese foreign policy – constraints and responses|first=Pedro Sanchez da Costa|last=Pereira|url=https://funag.gov.br/loja/download/the-road-ahead-livro-funag.pdf|page=281|access-date=24 April April 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20250625170259/http://www.idn.gov.pt/pt/publicacoes/nacao/Documents/NeD089/NeD89.pdf#page=11.00|archive-date=25 June 2025|url-status=live|trans-title=Portugal and Nato: 1949-1999}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.oecd.org/en/about/legal/text-of-the-convention-on-the-organisation-for-economic-co-operation-and-development.html|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240701192433/https://www.oecd.org/en/about/legal/text-of-the-convention-on-the-organisation-for-economic-co-operation-and-development.html|archive-date=1 July 2024|url-status =live|title=Convention on the Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development|author=Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development|publisher=self-published |access-date=29 April 2026}}</ref><ref name="EFTA">{{cite journal |last1=Andresen-Leitão |first1=Nicolau |title=O convidado inesperado: Portugal e a fundação da EFTA, 1956-1960 |trans-title=The Unexpected Guest: Portugal and the Founding of EFTA, 1956–1960 |language=pt |journal=Análise Social |date=2004 |volume=39 |issue=171 |pages=285–312 |jstor=41012368 |jstor-access=free }}</ref><ref>{{cite journal|url=https://biblat.unam.mx/hevila/CENAInternacional/2006/vol8/no1/3.pdf|access-date=24 April 2026|last=Freixo|first=Adriano de|title=Dez anos da CPLP: as perspectivas de integração do mundo de língua portuguesa|trans-title=Ten Years of the CPLP: the prospects for the integration of the Portuguese-speaking world|language=pt-BR|journal=Cena Internacional|type=Article|publication-date=June 2006|volume=8|issue=1|hdl=20.500.14330/CLA01000305636|pages=35–54|publication-place=Rio de Janeiro|publisher=Instituto Metodista Bennett|issn=1518-1200|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240715171222/https://biblat.unam.mx/hevila/CENAInternacional/2006/vol8/no1/3.pdf|archive-date=15 July 2024|url-status=live}}</ref>

Portugal has a stable foreign policy that is the result of its history, geography, and specific foreign policy choices. It is structured around six principal regional and policy priorities: Europe, NATO and relations with the [[Portugal–United Kingdom relations|United Kingdom]] and with the [[Portugal–United States relations|United States]], the [[Portuguese-speaking world]], the importance of and support for Portuguese communities abroad, the internationalization of the [[Economy of Portugal|national economy]], and the strengthening of [[multilateralism]]. Portugal regards the success of [[European integration]] as paramount and is prepared, where a consensus exists among European Union member states, to endorse policies that go against with the country's national interests;<ref>{{cite book|isbn= 978-85-7631-776-0 |title=The road ahead: the 21st-Century world order in the eyes of policy planners|oclc=1226359172|publication-place=Brasília|year=2018|publisher=Fundação Alexandre de Gusmão|editor-first1=Benoni|editor-last1=Belli|editor-first2=Filipe|editor-last2=Nasser|chapter=Portuguese foreign policy – constraints and responses|first=Pedro Sanchez da Costa|last=Pereira|url=https://funag.gov.br/loja/download/the-road-ahead-livro-funag.pdf|pages=269–283|access-date=24 April 2025|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230328233549/https://funag.gov.br/loja/download/the-road-ahead-livro-funag.pdf|archive-date=28 March 2023|url-status=live}}</ref> it also supports general disarmament, the dismantling of political-military blocs, and the creation of a collective security system aimed at establishing an international order grounded in peace and justice among peoples.<ref>{{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Fundamental principles |article= 7|clause=2|quote= Portugal advocates the abolition of imperialism, colonialism and any other forms of aggression, dominion and exploitation in the relations between peoples, as well as simultaneous and controlled general disarmament, the dissolution of the political-military blocs and the establishment of a collective security system, with a view to the creation of an international order that is capable of ensuring peace and justice in the relations between peoples.|edition=7th|access-date = 24 April 2026}}</ref>

Portugal has two territorial disputes, both of which are with Spain: the Spanish town of [[Olivenza]] which has been claimed by Portugal since the [[War of the Oranges|19th century]], and the Portuguese [[Savage Islands]] which have been claimed by Spain since 1911.<ref name="bie3">{{cite journal|url=https://www.ieee.es/Galerias/fichero/docs_opinion/2017/DIEEEO22-2017_IslasSalvajes_GomezAdeva.pdf |title=Las islas Salvajes: la mar como punto de encuentro |last=Gómez Adeva |first=Ana |publisher=Instituto Español de Estudios Estratégicos|journal=Boletín IEEE|pages=752–765|language=es|publication-place=Madrid|date=6 March 2017 |access-date=29 April 2026|eissn=2530-125X|issue=5 |archive-date=13 August 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230813175045/https://www.ieee.es/Galerias/fichero/docs_opinion/2017/DIEEEO22-2017_IslasSalvajes_GomezAdeva.pdf |url-status=live }}</ref> Despite causing moments of tension between the two countries, the [[Portugal–Spain relations|relationship between the two countries]] remains excellent.<ref name="bie3" /><ref>{{Cite web |title=Spain |url=https://portaldiplomatico.mne.gov.pt/en/bilateral-relations/general-countries/spain |access-date=29 April 2026|website=Diplomatic Portal |author=Ministry of Foreign Affairs|author-link=Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Portugal)|publisher=self-published|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260209132834/https://portaldiplomatico.mne.gov.pt/en/bilateral-relations/general-countries/spain|archive-date=9 February 2026|url-status=live}}</ref>

=== Military ===
{{Main|Portuguese Armed Forces}}

[[File:NRP Bartolomeu Dias F333 in Hernesaari as seen from Verkkokauppa in Helsinki, Finland, 2023 April.jpg|thumb|[[Portuguese Navy]] frigate NRP Bartolomeu Dias|alt=Photograph of NRP Bartolomeu Dias (F333) of the Portuguese Navy docked by the quays of Hernesaari, Helsinki, Finland, with the Portuguese flag flying at the stern and calm blue water stretching out to the open sea beyond.]]

The [[Portuguese Armed Forces]] consist of three branches commanded by the {{lang|pt-PT|[[Armed Forces General Staff (Portugal)|Estado-Maior-General das Forças Armadas]]}} (Armed Forces General Staff) – {{lang|pt-PT|[[Portuguese Navy|Marinha]]}} (Navy), {{lang|pt-PT|[[Portuguese Army|Exército]]}} (Army), and {{lang|pt-PT|[[Portuguese Air Force|Força Aérea]]}} (Air Force).<ref>{{cite act |author=Assembleia da República |trans-title=Organic Law No. 2/2021|at=No. 153/2021, Series 1|location={{lang|pt-PT|[[Diário da República]]}} |url=https://files.diariodarepublica.pt/1s/2021/08/15300/0000200017.pdf|access-date=29 April 2026|date=9 August 2021|language=pt-PT|title=Lei Orgânica n.º 2/2021|type= Organic Law}}</ref> In addition to the three branches of the armed forces, there is the {{lang|pt-PT|[[National Republican Guard (Portugal)|Guarda Nacional Republicana]]}} (National Republican Guard), a [[gendarmerie]], comprising {{Nts|23042}} personnel in 2025, under the authority of both the [[Ministry of National Defence (Portugal)|Defence]] and the [[Ministry of Home Affairs (Portugal)|Home Affairs]] ministries.<ref name="gnr">{{cite book|oclc=681908439|page=90|doi=10.1057/9780230599864_5|title=Policing Interwar Europe: Continuity, Change and Crisis, 1918–40|chapter=Guardians of the Republic?: Portugal's Guarda Nacional Republicana and the Politicians During the 'New Old Republic', 1919–22|publisher=Palgrave Macmillan|publication-place=London|isbn=978-0-230-59986-4|editor-first=Gerald|editor-last=Blaney Jr.|last1=Lloyd-Jones|last2=Cerezales|first1=Stewart|first2= Diego Palacios|date=2007}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.dgaep.gov.pt/upload/DIOEP/2025/SIEP3T/DGAEP-DIOEP_SIEP_2025_T3_20251114.xlsx|title=Q.1.5 Emprego no setor das administrações públicas por cargo/carreira/grupo, segundo o subsetor|author=DIOEP - Departamento de Informação da Organização do Estado e do Emprego Público|publisher=DGAEP - Direção-Geral da Administração e Emprego Público|date=14 November 2025|access-date=29 April 2026|language=pt-PT|trans-title=Q.1.5 Employment in the public administration sector, by post/career/group, according to subsector}}</ref> The Portuguese military serves as a self-defence force, takes part in humanitarian and peace missions undertaken by the international organisations to which Portugal belongs, and cooperates in civil defence missions.<ref>{{multiref2
|1={{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part III: Organisation of political power, Title X: National defence|article= 275|clause=1|quote=The Armed Forces are charged with the military defence of the Republic.|edition=7th|access-date = 25 April 2026}}
|2={{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part III: Organisation of political power, Title X: National defence|article= 275|clause=5|quote=The Armed Forces are charged, as laid down by law, with fulfilling the Portuguese state’s international commitments in the military field and taking part in humanitarian and peace missions undertaken by the international organisations to which Portugal belongs.|edition=7th|access-date = 25 April 2026}}
|3={{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part III: Organisation of political power, Title X: National defence|article= 275|clause=6|quote=The Armed Forces may be charged, as laid down by law, with cooperating in civil defence missions, tasks concerning the fulfilment of basic needs and the improvement of people's quality of life, and technical and military cooperation actions within the ambit of the national cooperation policy.|edition=7th|access-date = 25 April 2026}}}}</ref> In recent years, the Portuguese military have carried out several [[NATO]] and [[European Union]] missions worldwide.{{efn|Namely in [[Afghanistan]], [[Iraq]], [[Lebanon]], [[Bosnia and Herzegovina]], [[Kosovo]], [[Mali]], [[Central African Republic]], [[Somalia]], [[Mozambique]] and [[East Timor]].<ref>{{Cite web |title= Onde Estamos Missões No Estrangeiro|url=https://www.exercito.pt/pt/onde-estamos/no-mundo|author=Exército Português |access-date=29 April 2026|publisher=self-published|language=pt-PT|trans-title=Where We Are: Missions Abroad}}</ref>}} The [[List of countries by military expenditures|Portuguese military budget]] in 2025 was estimated at more than $6 billion, representing 2% of GDP.<ref>{{cite press release |author=North Atlantic Treaty Organisation |date= 28 August 2025|title=Defence Expenditure of NATO Countries (2014–2025)|url=https://www.nato.int/content/dam/nato/webready/documents/finance/def-exp-2025-en.pdf|location= Brussels|publisher=self-published|access-date=29 April 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260428110419/https://www.nato.int/content/dam/nato/webready/documents/finance/def-exp-2025-en.pdf|archive-date=28 April 2026|url-status=live}}</ref>

As of 2025, the three branches numbered {{Nts|23589}} military personnel.<ref>{{cite report|url=https://www.dgaep.gov.pt/upload//DIOEP/2025/SIEP3T/DGAEP%5FSIEP%5F2025T3%5F20251114.pdf|page=7|title=SIEP - Síntese estatística do emprego público|publisher=DGAEP - Direção-Geral da Administração e Emprego Público|author=DIOEP - Departamento de Informação da Organização do Estado e do Emprego Público|publication-date=14 November 2025|publication-place=Lisbon|language=pt-PT|trans-title=SIEP – Statistical Summary of Public Employment|issn=2182-7311}}</ref> Until 1999, military service was compulsory for men at age 18 becoming officially suspended during peace time and replaced by one mandatory day of sensibilization about the Armed Forces called {{lang|pt-PT|{{ill|National Defence Day (Portugal)|pt|Dia da Defesa Nacional|lt=Dia da Defesa Nacional}}}} (National Defence Day).<ref>{{cite journal|doi=10.4000/sociologico.103|title=O lugar do Dia da Defesa Nacional e a profissionalização das Forças Armadas: dilemas e desafios|journal=Forum Sociológico|access-date=26 April 2026|issn=2182-7427|url=https://journals.openedition.org/sociologico/103|publisher=CICS.NOVA – Interdisciplinary Centre of Social Sciences, NOVA School of Social Sciences and Humanities, NOVA University Lisbon|publication-place=Lisbon|publication-date= 1 June 2009|language=pt-PT|trans-title=The place of National Defence Day and the professionalisation of the Armed Forces: dilemmas and challenges|doi-access=free|first=José Manuel|last=Resende |volume=19 |pages=11–24 }}</ref> Since 1992 women may serve in all branches of the armed forces.<ref>{{cite report|author=Committee on Women in the NATO Forces|url=http://www.nato.int/ims/2008/win/reports/portugal-2008.pdf|title=Portugal|type=National report|publisher=NATO|publication-place=Brussels|date=1-6 June 2008|via=Wayback Machine|access-date=26 April 2026|pages=1–3 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080915153220/http://www.nato.int/ims/2008/win/reports/portugal-2008.pdf |archive-date=15 September 2008 }}</ref> The Portuguese military became fully professional in 2004.<ref>{{cite report|author=Committee on Women in the NATO Forces|url=http://www.nato.int/ims/2008/win/reports/portugal-2008.pdf|title=Portugal|type=National report|publisher=NATO|publication-place=Brussels|date=1-6 June 2008|via=Wayback Machine|access-date=26 April 2026|page=1 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080915153220/http://www.nato.int/ims/2008/win/reports/portugal-2008.pdf |archive-date=15 September 2008 }}</ref> The United States maintains a military presence, with 770 troops in the [[Lajes Air Base]] at [[Terceira Island]], in the Azores.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Base Aérea N.º 4 |url=https://www.emfa.pt/unidade-27-base-aerea-n-4 |access-date=29 April 2026|author=FAP - WEBTEAM|publisher=Força Aérea Portuguesa|language=pt-PT|trans-title=Air Base No. 4|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260226103610/https://www.emfa.pt/unidade-27-base-aerea-n-4|archive-date=26 February 2026|url-status=live}}</ref>

=== Law enforcement ===
{{Main|Law of Portugal|Judiciary of Portugal|Law enforcement in Portugal|Crime in Portugal}}

[[File:Polícia Judiciária (Portugal) headquarters, Lisbon 04.jpg|thumb|The headquarters of the {{lang|pt-PT|[[Polícia Judiciária]]}} (Judiciary Police), in Lisbon|alt=Photograph of the headquarters of the Judicial Police (PJ). A large modern white-and-grey office building with irregular window patterns stands on a corner under an overcast sky, with parked motorcycles, a few pedestrians, and a crosswalk in the foreground.]]

In Portugal, [[prosecution|public prosecution]] is conducted by the [[Public Prosecution Service (Portugal)|Public Prosecution Service]] which is headed by the {{ill|Prosecutor General of Portugal|pt|Procurador-Geral da República (Portugal)|lt=prosecutor general}}.<ref>{{cite book |last1=Narciso |first1=Madalena |title=Elgar Encyclopedia of Comparative Law |chapter=Portugal |date=2023 |pages=208–212 |doi=10.4337/9781839105609.portugal |isbn=978-1-83910-560-9 |oclc=1370217522 |lccn=2023945088 }}</ref> The main police organisations of Portugal are the {{lang|pt-PT|[[National Republican Guard (Portugal)|Guarda Nacional Republicana]]}} (National Republican Guard), the {{lang|pt-PT|[[Polícia de Segurança Pública]]}} (Public Security Police), a civilian police force that works in urban areas; and the {{lang|pt-PT|[[Polícia Judiciária]]}} (Judiciary Police), a senior criminal police body, under the authority of the [[Ministry of Justice (Portugal)|Minister of Justice]] and endowed with administrative autonomy.<ref name="gnr" /><ref>{{cite book|oclc=1047280619|title=Polícia e Polícias em Portugal: Perspetivas Históricas|isbn=978-989-8536-59-4|publication-place=Lisbon|publication-date=March 2017|edition=1st|publisher=Editora Mundos Sociais|language=pt-PT|trans-title=Police and Policing in Portugal: Historical Perspectives|page=4|chapter=Introdução: Perspetivas históricas sobre a polícia e o policiamento em Portugal|trans-chapter=Introduction: Historical perspectives on the police and policing in Portugal|first1=Gonçalo|last1=Rocha Gonçalves|first2=Susana|last2=Durão|url=https://www.susanadurao.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/Book-_-003.pdf|access-date=28 April 2026}}</ref><ref>{{cite journal|pages=189–193|publisher=Editorial Minerva|journal=Revista do Ministério Público|title=Órgãos de Polícia Criminal: o que são, os que são e os que não são|last=Cardoso|first=Rui|publication-date=23 March 2020|publication-place=Lisbon|url=https://rmp.smmp.pt/indice-do-no-161/|access-date=28 April 2026|issue=161|issn=0870-6107|language=pt-PT|trans-title=Criminal Police Bodies: what they are, which ones are, and which ones are not}}</ref>

Portugal has {{ill|List of prisons in Portugal|pt|Lista de prisões portuguesas|lt=49 correctional facilities}} run by the {{ill|Directorate-General for Reintegration and Prison Services|pt|Direção-Geral de Reinserção e Serviços Prisionais|lt=Directorate-General for Reintegration and Prison Services}} (DGRSP).<ref>{{cite web|url=https://dgrsp.justica.gov.pt/Justi%C3%A7a-de-adultos/Penas-e-medidas-privativas-de-liberdade/Estabelecimentos-prisionais|title=DGRSP > Justiça de adultos > Penas e medidas privativas de liberdade > Estabelecimentos prisionais|author=Direção Geral de Reinserção e Serviços Prisionais|publisher=self-published|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260308101322/https://dgrsp.justica.gov.pt/Justi%C3%A7a-de-adultos/Penas-e-medidas-privativas-de-liberdade/Estabelecimentos-prisionais|archive-date=8 March 2026|url-status=live|date=10 April 2024|language=pt-PT|trans-title=DGRSP > Justice of adults > Sentences and restrictive measures of liberty > Correctional facilities|access-date=February 28, 2026}}</ref> The facilities include seventeen central prisons, four special prisons, twenty-seven regional prisons, and one ''Cadeia de Apoio'' (Support Detention Centre).<ref>{{cite web|url=http://prisonstudies.org/country/portugal|title=Portugal {{!}} World Prison Brief|author=World Prison Brief|publisher=Institute for Crime & Justice Policy Research|access-date=29 April 2026|archive-date=24 April 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190424155203/http://prisonstudies.org/country/portugal|url-status=live}}</ref> As of 2024, the prison population stood at {{Nts|12193}} inmates, with the incarceration rate increasing between 2023 and 2024.<ref>{{cite web|doi=10.2908/CRIM_PRIS_CAP|doi-access=free|title=Prison capacity and number of persons held|author=Eurostat|publisher=self-published|date=29 March 2026|url=https://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/databrowser/bookmark/5143162e-5dea-4b9a-ae1a-22a22ca6e074?lang=en|access-date=29 April 2026}}</ref><ref>{{cite report|title=Council of Europe Annual Penal Statistics: Prison populations|url=https://wp.unil.ch/space/files/2025/09/250924_rapport-space-i-2024.pdf|page=37|first1=Marcelo F.|last1=Aebi|first2=Edoardo|last2=Cocco|publication-place=Strasbourg|publication-date=24 September 2025|id=PC-CP (2024) 5|publisher=Council of Europe|access-date=29 April 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260116174357/https://wp.unil.ch/space/files/2025/09/250924_rapport-space-i-2024.pdf|archive-date=16 January 2026|url-status=live}}</ref>

=== Human rights ===
{{Main|Human rights in Portugal}}

Portugal has a tradition of a humanistic criminal justice.<ref name="UCILeR">{{cite report|publisher=University of Coimbra Institute for Legal Research (UCILeR)|first1=Anabela|last1=Miranda Rodrigues|first2=Maria|last2=João Antunes|first3=Sónia|last3=Fidalgo|first4=Inês|last4=Horta Pinto|first5=Karla Tayumi|last5=Ishiy|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260428121309/https://www.uc.pt/site/assets/files/422661/portugal.pdf|archive-date=28 April 2026|url-status=live|url=https://www.uc.pt/site/assets/files/422661/portugal.pdf|access-date=14 April 2026|publication-place=Coimbra, Portugal|publication-date=November 2021|title=Promoting non-discriminatory alternatives toimprisonment across Europe|page=1}}</ref> The [[Constitution of Portugal|Portuguese Constitution]] defines the country as being one that is based on human dignity.<ref>{{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Fundamental principles |article= 1|quote= Portugal is a sovereign Republic, based on the dignity of the human person and the will of the people and committed to building a free, just and solidary society.|edition=7th|access-date = 15 April 2026}}</ref> It abolished [[capital punishment]] and [[life imprisonment]] in the 19th century,<ref name=UCILeR/> and forbids [[extradition]] in the case of either sentence possibly being imposed.<ref>{{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part I: Fundamental rights and duties, Title II: Rights, freedoms and guarantees, Chapter I: Personal rights, freedoms and guarantees |article= 33|clause=4|quote= Extradition for crimes that are punishable under the applicant state’s law by a sentence or security measure which deprives or restricts freedom in perpetuity or for an undefined duration, is only permissible if the applicant state is a party to an international convention in this domain to which Portugal is bound, and offers guarantees that such a sentence or security measure will not be applied or executed.|edition=7th|access-date = 15 April 2026}}</ref><ref>{{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part I: Fundamental rights and duties, Title II: Rights, freedoms and guarantees, Chapter I: Personal rights, freedoms and guarantees |article= 33|clause=6|quote= The extradition or handing over of a person under any circumstances for political reasons, or for crimes which are punishable under the applicant state’s law by death or by any other sentence that results in irreversible damage to physical integrity, is not permitted.|edition=7th|access-date = 15 April 2026}}</ref> Portugal is the only country that considers any type of punishment for the duration of a convict's natural life a violation of [[human rights]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://eu2021.justica.gov.pt/en-gb/News/Life-imprisonment-has-no-positive-sense-of-reintegration|title=Life imprisonment has no positive sense of reintegration|website=EU2021|author=Ministério da Justiça|publisher=Secretaria-Geral do Ministério da Justiça|author-link=Ministry of Justice (Portugal)|date=9 March 2021|access-date=29 April 2026|url-status= live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20250806163947/https://eu2021.justica.gov.pt/en-gb/News/Life-imprisonment-has-no-positive-sense-of-reintegration|archive-date= August 6, 2025}}</ref> The [[Portuguese Penal Code]] provides for a wide range of non-custodial sentences, with the aim of keeping a prison sentence a punishment of last resort. Portuguese penitentiary laws have traditionally been progressive, and based on rehabilitation as the main goal of the implementation of such a sentence.<ref name=UCILeR/>

Since the 2000s, numerous laws strengthening [[LGBTQ rights in Portugal|LGBT rights]] were passed in Portugal.{{efn|In 2003, Portugal added an anti-discrimination employment law on the basis of [[LGBTQ rights in Portugal|sexual orientation]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.pgdlisboa.pt/leis/lei_mostra_articulado.php?nid=441&tabela=lei_velhas&nversao=1&so_miolo=|title=Lei n.º 99/2003, de 27 de Agosto|website=pgdlisboa.pt|access-date=8 December 2019|archive-date=6 August 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200806093208/http://www.pgdlisboa.pt/leis/lei_mostra_articulado.php?nid=441&tabela=lei_velhas&nversao=1&so_miolo=|url-status=live}}</ref>}}{{efn|In 2004, sexual orientation was added to the Constitution as part of the protected from discrimination characteristics.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.pgdlisboa.pt/leis/lei_mostra_articulado.php?nid=79&tabela=leis&ficha=1&pagina=1&so_miolo=|title=Lei n.º 1/2004, de 24 de Julho|website=pgdlisboa.pt|access-date=8 December 2019|archive-date=1 May 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200501183704/http://www.pgdlisboa.pt/leis/lei_mostra_articulado.php?nid=79&tabela=leis&ficha=1&pagina=1&so_miolo=|url-status=live}}</ref>}}{{efn|In 2010, Portugal became the sixth country in Europe and eighth in the world to legalise [[same-sex marriage in Portugal|same-sex marriage]] at the national level.<ref name="autogenerated2">{{cite web|url=http://dre.pt/pdf1sdip/2010/05/10500/0185301853.pdf|title=Diário da República, 1.ª série — N.º 105 — 31 May 2010|access-date=14 September 2013|archive-date=6 January 2014|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140106163651/https://dre.pt/pdf1sdip/2010/05/10500/0185301853.pdf|url-status=live}}</ref>}}{{efn|[[LGBT adoption]] was legalized in 2016<ref>{{cite web|url=http://app.parlamento.pt/webutils/docs/doc.pdf?path=6148523063446f764c3246795a5868774d546f334e7a67774c336470626e526c654852766331396863484a76646d466b62334d764d6a41784e69394d587a4a664d6a41784e6935775a47593d&fich=L_2_2016.pdf&Inline=true|title=Lei n.º 2/2016 de 29 de fevereiro|website=App.parlamento.pt|access-date=11 April 2017|archive-date=27 September 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180927181934/http://app.parlamento.pt/webutils/docs/doc.pdf?path=6148523063446f764c3246795a5868774d546f334e7a67774c336470626e526c654852766331396863484a76646d466b62334d764d6a41784e69394d587a4a664d6a41784e6935775a47593d&fich=L_2_2016.pdf&Inline=true|url-status=live}}</ref> as has female same-sex couple access to medically assisted reproduction.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://rr.sapo.pt/noticia/54117/parlamento_aprova_barrigas_de_aluguer_e_procriacao_medicamente_assistida|title=Parlamento aprova barrigas de aluguer e Procriação Medicamente Assistida – Renascença|last=Renascença|website=rr.sapo.pt|date=13 May 2016|access-date=11 April 2017|archive-date=30 June 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190630063804/http://rr.sapo.pt/noticia/54117/parlamento_aprova_barrigas_de_aluguer_e_procriacao_medicamente_assistida|url-status=live}}</ref>}}{{efn|In 2017 the ''Law of Gender Identity'',<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://expresso.sapo.pt/sociedade/2016-12-31-Nova-lei-vai-permitir-mudanca-de-sexo-a-menores|title=Governo entrega em janeiro projeto da nova Lei da Identidade de Género, que prevê a descida da idade legal e o fim do atestado médico obrigatório|website=Expresso.sapo.pt|access-date=29 July 2018|archive-date=4 July 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180704003548/http://expresso.sapo.pt/sociedade/2016-12-31-Nova-lei-vai-permitir-mudanca-de-sexo-a-menores}}</ref> simplified the legal process of [[gender]] and name change for [[transgender]] people, making it easier for minors to change their [[sex marker]] in legal documents.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.dn.pt/sociedade/interior/375-pessoas-mudaram-de-genero-no-registo-civil-5590815.html|title=Dário de Notícias: 375 pessoas mudaram de género no registo civil|date=1 July [[gender identity]] and [[gender expression]] self-determination became protected, [[intersex]] minors became protected by law from unnecessary [[Intersex medical interventions|medical procedures]] "until the minor gender identity manifests" and the right of protection from discrimination on the basis of [[Sex characteristics (legal term)|sex characteristics]] became protected by the same law.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://dre.pt/web/guest/pesquisa/-/search/115933863/details/maximized|title=Lei 38/2018, 2018-08-07|website=Diário da República Eletrónico|language=pt|access-date=8 December 2019|archive-date=8 December 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191208131252/https://dre.pt/web/guest/pesquisa/-/search/115933863/details/maximized|url-status=live}}</ref>}} In 2001, Portugal became the first country in the world to [[Drug policy of Portugal|decriminalize]] the personal possession and consumption of all drugs.<ref>{{Cite journal |last1=Rêgo|first1=Ximene |last2=Oliveira|first2=Maria João |last3=Lameira|first3=Catarina |last4=Cruz|first4=Olga S. |date=17 July 2021 |title=20 years of Portuguese drug policy - developments, challenges and the quest for human rights |journal=Substance Abuse Treatment, Prevention, and Policy |volume=16 |issue=1 |page=59 |doi=10.1186/s13011-021-00394-7 |doi-access=free |pmc=8285857 |pmid=34273972}}</ref> Portugal faces issues such as police brutality,<ref>{{cite report|author=European Committee for the Prevention of Torture and Inhuman or Degrading Treatment or Punishment (CPT)|publisher=self-published|docket=CPT/Inf (2025) 32|access-date=17 April 2026|url=https://rm.coe.int/2024/488028f8a1|pages=8–14|publication-date=21 October 2015|publication-place=Strasbourg|title=Visit report - Portugal - November 2024}}</ref> widespread racism and discrimination against minorities,<ref name="immigrationPress">{{cite press release |author=Statistics Portugal|author-link=Instituto Nacional de Estatística (Portugal) |date= 22 December 2023|title=Survey on Living Conditions, Origins and Trajectories of the Resident Population 2023|url=https://www.ine.pt/xportal/xmain?xpid=INE&xpgid=ine_destaques&DESTAQUESdest_boui=625453018&DESTAQUESmodo=2&xlang=en|location= Lisbon, Portugal|publisher=self-published|access-date=25 April 2026}}</ref> {{ill|Slavery in contemporary Portugal|pt|Escravatura moderna em Portugal|lt=migrant slavery}},<ref>{{cite web|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260226071501/https://www.state.gov/reports/2025-trafficking-in-persons-report/portugal/|archive-date=26 February 2026|url-status=live|url=https://www.state.gov/reports/2025-trafficking-in-persons-report/portugal/|title=2025 Trafficking in Persons Report: Portugal|author=United States Department of State - Bureau of Democracy, Human Rights, and Labor - Office to Monitor and Combat Trafficking in Persons|publisher=United States Department of State|publication-date=30 September 2025|access-date=29 April 2026}}</ref> restrictions on freedom of association and collective bargaining,<ref>{{cite report|title=Portugal 2024 Human Rights Report|url=https://www.state.gov/wp-content/uploads/2025/07/62451_PORTUGAL-2024-HUMAN-RIGHTS-REPORT.pdf|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20250812204744/https://www.state.gov/wp-content/uploads/2025/07/62451_PORTUGAL-2024-HUMAN-RIGHTS-REPORT.pdf|archive-date=12 August 2025|url-status=live|publisher= United States Department of State|department=Section 2. Liberty|chapter=b. Worker Rights|page=3|series=Country Reports on Human Rights Practices for 2024|author=United States Department of State - Bureau of Democracy, Human Rights, and Labor}}</ref> violations of wage, hour, and overtime laws,<ref>{{cite report|title=Portugal 2024 Human Rights Report|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20250812204744/https://www.state.gov/wp-content/uploads/2025/07/62451_PORTUGAL-2024-HUMAN-RIGHTS-REPORT.pdf|archive-date=12 August 2025|url-status=live|url=https://www.state.gov/wp-content/uploads/2025/07/62451_PORTUGAL-2024-HUMAN-RIGHTS-REPORT.pdf|publisher= United States Department of State|department=Section 2.
