Worker Rights|page=5|series=Country Reports on Human Rights Practices for 2024|author=United States Department of State - Bureau of Democracy, Human Rights, and Labor}}</ref> and treatment inside prisons.<ref>{{cite report|author=European Committee for the Prevention of Torture and Inhuman or Degrading Treatment or Punishment (CPT)|publisher=self-published|docket=CPT/Inf (2025) 32|publication-place=Strasbourg|access-date=17 April 2026|url=https://rm.coe.int/2024/488028f8a1|pages=15–21|publication-date=21 October 2015|title=Visit report - Portugal - November 2024}}</ref>

== Economy ==
<!-- If you want to expand this section, please instead add new info into the main article: "Economy of Portugal", your work there will be appreciated. -->
{{Main|Economy of Portugal}}

[[File:Lisboa June 2014-14a.jpg|thumb|[[Parque das Nações]], in Lisbon; an economic centre in Portugal|alt=Photography of Parque das Nações, in Lisbon. Modern waterfront buildings, including two tall glass-and-concrete towers with sail-shaped white roofs, can be seen across the Tagus River under a blue sky with few thin white clouds. Trees, a riverside promenade, pedestrians, and nearby commercial buildings line the waterfront.]]

Portugal is a [[high-income country]] with an [[advanced economy]] that follows the [[European social model#Mediterranean model|Mediterranean model]].<ref>{{cite web |url=https://datahelpdesk.worldbank.org/knowledgebase/articles/906519-world-bank-country-and-lending-groups |title=World Bank Country and Lending Groups |author=World Bank Group|publisher=self-published|website=World Bank Open Data|publication-place=Washington, D.C. |access-date=29 April 2026}}</ref><ref>{{cite journal|eissn=1564-5215|issn= 0256-6877|journal=World Economic and Financial Surveys|title=World Economic Outlook: Global Economy in the Shadow of War|isbn=979-8-22904-278-9|publication-place=Washington, D.C.|publication-date=14 April 2026|author=International Monetary Fund|publisher=self-published|page=99|url=https://www.imf.org/-/media/files/publications/weo/2026/april/english/text.pdf|access-date=30 April 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260423140612/https://www.imf.org/-/media/files/publications/weo/2026/april/english/text.pdf|archive-date=23 April 2026|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite journal|page=181|journal=Athens Journal of Mediterranean Studies|volume=6|issue=3|date=July 2020|doi=10.30958/ajms.6-3-1|doi-access=free|last= Gentilucci|first=Catia Eliana|publisher=Athens Institute for Education & Research|publication-place=Athens|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20251001131738/https://www.athensjournals.gr/mediterranean/2020-6-3-1-Gentilucci.pdf|archive-date=1 October 2025|url-status=live|eissn=2407-9480|title=The Mediterranean Model in European Economic Thought|access-date=16 April 2026|url=https://www.athensjournals.gr/mediterranean/2020-6-3-1-Gentilucci.pdf}}</ref> The country's economic policy is framed by strategic guidelines called {{ill|Major Plan Options|pt|Grandes Opções do Plano|lt=Major Plan Options}}, which are subsequently implemented through the [[government budget|State Budget]].<ref>{{multiref2 
|1={{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part II: Organisation of the economy, Title II: Plans|article= 90|quote=The objective of economic and social development plans shall be to promote economic growth, the harmonious and integrated development of sectors and regions, the just division of the national product between persons and between regions, the coordination of the economic policy with the social, education and cultural policies, the defence of the rural world, the preservation of the ecological balance, the defence of the environment and the quality of life of the Portuguese people.|edition=7th|access-date = 23 April 2026}}
|2={{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part II: Organisation of the economy, Title IV: Financial and fiscal system|article= 105|clause=2|quote=The Budget shall be drawn up in harmony with the major planning options and in the light of legal and contractual obligations.|edition=7th|access-date = 23 April 2026}}
|3={{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part II: Organisation of the economy, Title IV: Financial and fiscal system|article= 105|clause=3|quote=The Budget shall be a single budget and shall set out expenditure in accordance with the respective organisational and functional classification, in such a way as to preclude the existence of secret appropriations and funds. It may also be structured by programmes.|edition=7th|access-date = 23 April 2026}}}}</ref> Portugal has the EU's [[List of sovereign states in Europe by GDP (nominal)|14th-largest economy by nominal GDP]] and the [[List of sovereign states in Europe by GDP (PPP)|12th-largest economy by PPP-adjusted GDP]].<ref>{{cite journal|eissn=1564-5215|issn= 0256-6877|journal=World Economic and Financial Surveys|title=World Economic Outlook: Global Economy in the Shadow of War|isbn=979-8-22904-278-9|publication-place=Washington, D.C.|publication-date=14 April 2026|author=International Monetary Fund|publisher=self-published|page=39|url=https://www.imf.org/-/media/files/publications/weo/2026/april/english/text.pdf|access-date=30 April 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260423140612/https://www.imf.org/-/media/files/publications/weo/2026/april/english/text.pdf|archive-date=23 April 2026|url-status=live}}</ref> Its PPP-adjusted GDP per capita stood at to 81% of the EU average in 2025.<ref>{{cite web|doi=10.2908/PRC_PPP_IND_1|doi-access=free|title=Purchasing power parities, price level indices, nominal and real expenditures by analytical categories - based on COICOP 2018|url=https://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/databrowser/bookmark/ecfbff41-69cb-47d9-bb89-bdb52711fcd4?lang=en|publication-date=25 March 2026|author=Eurostat|publisher=self-published|access-date=30 April 2026}}</ref> As of 2024, the country's service sector contributes the most for its economic output followed the industrial sector and its [[primary sector]].<ref name="sectorsGDP">{{cite web|title=Statistics Portugal - Data Base - Indicator 0006612|author=Statistics Portugal|author-link=Instituto Nacional de Estatística (Portugal)|publisher=self-published|publication-date=11 December 2025|access-date=30 April 2026|url=https://www.ine.pt/xportal/xmain?xpid=INE&xpgid=ine_indicadores&indOcorrCod=0006612&contexto=bd&selTab=tab2&xlang=en}}</ref> In 2025, Portugal [[List of countries by unemployment rate|unemployment rate]] was 5.8%.<ref>{{cite press release |author=Statistics Portugal|author-link=Instituto Nacional de Estatística (Portugal) |date= 4 February 2026|issn=2184-4534|title=Employment statistics – 4th quarter of 2025|url=https://www.ine.pt/xportal/xmain?xpid=INE&xpgid=ine_destaques&DESTAQUESdest_boui=706224094&DESTAQUESmodo=2|location= Lisbon|publisher=self-published|access-date=30 April 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260312015643/https://www.ine.pt/ngt_server/attachfileu.jsp?look_parentBoui=775302370&att_display=n&att_download=y|archive-date=12 March 2026|url-status=live}}</ref> As of 2024, its poverty rate after social transfers is 15.4% of the population while in 2023, the at-risk-of-poverty rate before social transfers stood at 40.3%.<ref>{{cite press release |author=Statistics Portugal|author-link=Instituto Nacional de Estatística (Portugal) |date= 11 December 2025|issn=2184-4534|title=Income and Living Conditions – 2025|url=https://www.ine.pt/xportal/xmain?xpid=INE&xpgid=ine_destaques&DESTAQUESdest_boui=707495469&DESTAQUESmodo=2|location= Lisbon|publisher=self-published|access-date=30 April 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20251211173428/https://www.ine.pt/ngt_server/attachfileu.jsp?look_parentBoui=765653587&att_display=n&att_download=y|archive-date=11 December 2025|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{Cite journal|title=Tendências recentes da pobreza e da privação em Portugal: O agravamento na população idosa e nas mulheres|url=https://www.observatorio-das-desigualdades.com/2025/01/13/tendencias-recentes-da-pobreza-e-da-privacao-em-portugal-de-ines-tavares-e-renato-miguel-do-carmo|doi=10.15847/CIESODPobrezaPrivacao2024|doi-access=free|publication-place=Lisbon|page=13|last1=Tavares|first1=Inês|last2=Carmo|first2=Renato Miguel do|journal=Inequality Observatory|publisher=CIES-Iscte|year=2025|trans-title=Recent trends in poverty and deprivation in Portugal: The worsening situation among the elderly population and women|language=pt-PT|access-date=18 March 2026}}</ref> The percentage of the Portuguese population suffering from moderate or severe [[food insecurity]] between 2022 and 2024 was on average 11.9%, which makes Portugal the third-highest country in [[Southern Europe]] for this indicator where the average stands at 5.9%.<ref>{{Cite report|series=The State of Food Security and Nutrition in the World (SOFI)|title=The State of Food Security and Nutrition in the World 2025 – Addressing high food price inflation for food security and nutrition|year=2025|oclc=1534873607|author1=FAO|author2= IFAD|author3=UNICEF|author4=WFP|author5= WHO|publisher=self-published|doi=10.4060/cd6008en|url=https://openknowledge.fao.org/handle/20.500.14283/cd6008en|access-date=February 2, 2026|isbn=978-92-5-139937-8|issn=2663-8061|eissn=2663-807X|location=Rome|page=120|doi-access=free|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260403070855/https://openknowledge.fao.org/server/api/core/bitstreams/e3c60970-7123-4de4-9d82-81f4a08912e4/content|archive-date=3 April 2026|url-status =live}}</ref> The [[Portuguese national debt|national debt of Portugal]] is estimated at 89.5% relative to GDP as of 2025.<ref>{{cite press release |author=Statistics Portugal|author-link=Instituto Nacional de Estatística (Portugal) |date= 26 March 2026|issn=2184-4534|title=Excessive deficit procedure: 1st notification 2026|url=https://www.ine.pt/xportal/xmain?xpid=INE&xpgid=ine_destaques&DESTAQUESdest_boui=762272780&DESTAQUESmodo=2|location= Lisbon|publisher=self-published|access-date=30 April 2026}}</ref>

Portugal is part of the [[European single market]] which represents more than 450 million consumers.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://ec.europa.eu/growth/single-market_en|title=The European single market|date=5 July 2016|author=European Commission|publisher=self-published|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200409110216/https://ec.europa.eu/growth/single-market_en|archive-date=9 April 2020|url-status=live|access-date=16 April 2026}}</ref> Portugal replaced the [[Portuguese escudo|escudo]] with the [[euro]] in 2002.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.ecb.europa.eu/euro/changeover/2002/html/index.en.html|publisher=self-published|access-date=16 April 2026|title=Initial changeover (2002)|date=31 January 2023|author=European Central Bank|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260420131848/https://www.ecb.europa.eu/euro/changeover/2002/html/index.en.html|archive-date=20 April 2026|url-status=live}}</ref> Its monetary policy is set by the [[European Central Bank]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.bportugal.pt/en/page/what-monetary-policy-and-what-it-used|author=Banco de Portugal|publisher=self-published|access-date=16 April 2026|title=What is monetary policy and what is it used for?|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20250831070832/https://www.bportugal.pt/en/page/what-monetary-policy-and-what-it-used|archive-date=31 August 2025|url-status=live}}</ref> The country has been a part of the [[Eurozone]] since its inception.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://economy-finance.ec.europa.eu/euro/what-euro-area_en|title=What is the euro area?|author=European Commission|access-date=16 April 2026|website=Economy and Finance|publisher=self-published|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260331235803/https://economy-finance.ec.europa.eu/euro/what-euro-area_en|archive-date=31 March 2026|url-status=live}}</ref> Portugal's [[central bank]] is the [[Banco de Portugal]] and it is part of the [[European System of Central Banks]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.bportugal.pt/en/page/eurosystemescb|title=Eurosystem/ESCB|author=Banco de Portugal|publisher=self-published|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20250824125004/https://www.bportugal.pt/en/page/eurosystemescb|archive-date=24 August 2025|url-status=live|access-date=16 April 2026}}</ref> In 2024, Portugal had a combined share of exports and imports that amounted to 90% of its total GDP.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://data.worldbank.org/indicator/NE.TRD.GNFS.ZS |title=Trade (% of GDP) |author=World Bank Group|publisher=self-published|publication-place=Washington, D.C. |access-date=30 April 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260425212634/https://data.worldbank.org/indicator/NE.TRD.GNFS.ZS|archive-date=25 April 2026|url-status=live}}</ref> As of February 2026, Portugal's main export markets were Spain at 26% and Germany at 13.9%.<ref name="ExportsImports">{{cite press release |author=Statistics Portugal|author-link=Instituto Nacional de Estatística (Portugal) |date= 9 April 2026|issn=2184-4534|title=International trade – February 2026|url=https://www.ine.pt/xportal/xmain?xpid=INE&xpgid=ine_destaques&DESTAQUESdest_boui=768240472&DESTAQUESmodo=2&xlang=en|location= Lisbon|publisher=self-published|access-date=30 April 2026}}</ref> Its main exports are machinery and mechanical appliances, vehicles and other transportation equipment, base metals, and plastics.<ref name="ExportsImports" /> Portugal's main import markets in 2026 were Spain at 32.9% and Germany at 11.9%.<ref name ="ExportsImports" /> Portugal's main imports are machinery and mechanical appliances, chemical products, agricultural products, and mineral fuels.<ref name ="ExportsImports" />

Since the 1990s, Portugal's economic model has been based on [[consumption (economics)|public consumption]] and [[economic development]] focused on exports, private [[investment (macroeconomics)|investment]] and the development of its [[high-tech]] sector. Consequently, business services have overtaken more traditional industries such as [[wine]] and [[Cork (material)|cork]] in export earnings.<ref name="autogenerated1">{{cite report|publication-place=London|title=Financial Times Special Report: Investing in Portugal|url=https://im.ft-static.com/content/images/c6e46b22-7b6f-11e4-87d4-00144feabdc0.pdf|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151008231201/http://im.ft-static.com/content/images/c6e46b22-7b6f-11e4-87d4-00144feabdc0.pdf|archive-date=8 October 2015|url-status=live|author=Financial Times|publisher=self-published|access-date=16 April 2026|date=5 December 2014|page=4}}</ref> The [[PSI-20|PSI]], Portugal's stock market index operated by the [[Euronext Lisbon]], includes 16 major Portugal-based companies. Preeminent Portuguese companies include [[Sonae]], [[Mota-Engil]], [[Corticeira Amorim]], [[The Navigator Company]] and [[EDP Group|EDP]].<ref name="psi">{{cite web|url=https://live.euronext.com/en/markets/lisbon/equities-by-index/psi|title=PSI Stocks|author=Euronext|publisher=self-published|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260130012145/https://live.euronext.com/en/markets/lisbon/equities-by-index/psi|archive-date=30 January 2026|url-status=live|access-date=16 April 2026}}</ref>

In 2025, Portugal ranked 16th among European Union member states in innovation by the [[European Innovation Scoreboard]], while placing 31st worldwide in the [[Global Innovation Index]].<ref>{{cite report|author=European Commission: Directorate-General for Research and Innovation|publisher=Publications Office of the European Union|doi=10.2777/3239776|docket=KI-01-25-136-EN-N|title=European Innovation Scoreboard 2025|isbn=978-92-68-28502-2|publication-place=Luxembourg|publication-date=15 July 2025|issn=2467-4435|series=European innovation scoreboard|edition=14th|url=https://op.europa.eu/en/publication-detail/-/publication/c102236e-66b2-11f0-bf4e-01aa75ed71a1/language-en|access-date=30 April 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20250715224653/https://research-and-innovation.ec.europa.eu/document/download/3d4f12c2-033e-451b-9c4c-0d28c0339cfe_en|archive-date=15 July 2025|url-status=live|page=71|doi-access=free}}</ref><ref>{{cite report|oclc=1583219854|author=World Intellectual Property Organization (WIPO) |title=Global Innovation Index 2025: Innovation at a Crossroads|publisher=self-published|doi=10.34667/tind.58864|isbn= 978-92-805-3797-0|issn= 2263-3693|eissn= 2788-6972 |publication-place=Geneva|url=https://www.wipo.int/web-publications/global-innovation-index-2025/assets/89507/global-innovation-index-2025-en.pdf|page=68|access-date=30 April 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260226190553/https://www.wipo.int/web-publications/global-innovation-index-2025/assets/89507/global-innovation-index-2025-en.pdf|archive-date=26 February 2026|url-status=live|doi-access=free|edition=18th|series=Global Innovation Index|publication-date=16 September 2025}}</ref> In 2024, neuroscience accounted for 12.5% of Portugal's scientific output, the second-highest national share, and the country ranked 23rd worldwide in total neuroscience output.<ref>{{cite journal |title=High-performers and specialists in neuroscience research |journal=Nature |date=3 October 2024 |volume=634 |issue=8032 |pages=S7 |doi=10.1038/d41586-024-03045-6 |pmid=39358538 |bibcode=2024Natur.634S...7. }}</ref> Among the research institutions based in the country are the [[Gulbenkian Institute of Molecular Medicine]], the [[International Iberian Nanotechnology Laboratory]], and the [[Champalimaud Foundation]] which was the world's eleventh top non-profit institution in neuroscience research between 2019 and 2023.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Leading 25 NPO/NGO institutions|author=Nature Index| publisher=Nature Portfolio|date=2 October 2024 |access-date=30 April 2026|url=https://www.nature.com/nature-index/supplements/nature-index-2024-neuroscience/tables/npo-ngo}}</ref>

=== Agriculture and fishery ===
{{main|Agriculture in Portugal|Fishing industry in Portugal}}

[[File:Ameixial - cork store (13532168205).jpg|thumb|The harvesting of [[Cork (material)|cork]] bark. More than half of the world's cork is produced in Portugal.<ref>{{cite report|pages=19–20|first1=Vasco|last1=Rodrigues|first2=Eylem|last2=Gevrek|first3=Filipa|last3=Mota|title=The Cork Sector: Description|publisher= Associação Portuguesa da Cortiça|publication-date=June 2023|publication-place=Santa Maria de Lamas|url=https://apcor.pt/uploads/Media/Estudos/estudo-tecnologico-2023/3_O%20Setor%20da%20Cortic%CC%A7a_Caracterizac%CC%A7a%CC%83o_EN.pdf|access-date=4 May 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260504232443/https://apcor.pt/uploads/Media/Estudos/estudo-tecnologico-2023/3_O%20Setor%20da%20Cortic%CC%A7a_Caracterizac%CC%A7a%CC%83o_EN.pdf|archive-date=4 May 2026|url-status=live}}</ref>]]

The Portuguese agriculture sector accounts for 2.9% of the country's total GDP as of 2024.<ref name="sectorsGDP" /> Portugal's [[agricultural land]] encompasses an area of approximately {{convert|3697000|ha|km2|0|abbr=on}} as of 2023, of which 17.4% is dedicated to [[organic farming]], representing the fifth-highest share worldwide.<ref>{{cite book|pages=45,348,368|doi=10.4060/cd4313en|doi-access=free|publication-place=Rome|isbn=978-92-5-140174-3|title=World Food and Agriculture – Statistical Yearbook 2025|author=FAO|publisher=self-published|series=FAO Statistical Yearbook – World Food and Agriculture|issn=2225-7373|oclc=1583153409|publication-date=2025|url=https://openknowledge.fao.org/server/api/core/bitstreams/ece7c683-4659-4fd0-b958-4bcbe8654cf7/content|access-date=1 May 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20251214203849/https://openknowledge.fao.org/server/api/core/bitstreams/ece7c683-4659-4fd0-b958-4bcbe8654cf7/content|archive-date=14 December 2025|url-status=live}}</ref> Despite the extent of the country's agricultural land, the diversity of Portugal's [[Edaphology|edaphoclimatic]] and [[Agroecology|agroecological]] conditions enables the cultivation of various agricultural products such wheat, maize, rice with each one having an important role in the primary sector, and resulting in an agricultural self-sufficiency rate of 85% as of 2018.<ref>{{cite journal|last1=Viana |first1=Cláudia M. |last2=Freire |first2=Dulce |last3=Abrantes |first3=Patrícia |last4=Rocha |first4=Jorge |title=Evolution of Agricultural Production in Portugal during 1850–2018: A Geographical and Historical Perspective|issn=2073-445X|doi=10.3390/land10080776|doi-access=free|department=Introduction|publication-date=23 July 2021|journal=Land|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220802122059/https://mdpi-res.com/d_attachment/land/land-10-00776/article_deploy/land-10-00776.pdf?version=1627035629|archive-date=2 August 2022|url-status=live|publication-place=Basel|access-date=17 April 2026|volume=10|issue=8|page=776 |publisher=Multidisciplinary Digital Publishing Institute|bibcode=2021Land...10..776V |type=Article|url=https://www.mdpi.com/2073-445X/10/8/776/pdf?version=1627035629}}</ref><ref>{{cite report|pages=75–76|publication-date=July 2021|title=Plano Estratégico da PAC 2023-2027 – Diagnóstico|author=Gabinete de Planeamento, Políticas e Administração Geral|url=https://www.gpp.pt/images/PEPAC/Documentos_PEPAC/Diagn%C3%B3stico_OE2.pdf|publication-place=Lisbon|publisher=[[Ministry of Agriculture (Portugal)|Ministry of Agriculture]]|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20241117191700/https://www.gpp.pt/images/PEPAC/Documentos_PEPAC/Diagn%C3%B3stico_OE2.pdf|archive-date=17 November 2024|access-date=1 May 2026|url-status=live|language=pt-PT|trans-title=Strategic Plan for the PAC 2023–2027 – Diagnosis}}</ref>

Portugal ranks sixth in the world in [[List of countries by seafood consumption|seafood consumption per capita]] with each Portuguese consuming on average {{convert|54|kg|lb|0|abbr=on}} of fish in 2023.<ref>{{cite book|page=92|doi=10.4060/cd6788en|doi-access=free|publication-place=Rome|isbn=978-92-5-140095-1|title=Fishery and Aquaculture Statistics – Yearbook 2023|author=FAO|publisher=self-published|series=FAO Yearbook of Fishery and Aquaculture Statistics|issn=2960-0499|eissn=2960-0502|oclc=1583153409|publication-date=22 October 2025|url=https://openknowledge.fao.org/server/api/core/bitstreams/140be7f8-74b2-4b8a-9ca7-285719c31e53/content|access-date=1 May 2026}}</ref> The high fish consumption in Portugal is due to tradition and cultural roots, politics, dynamics of the fish market system, and geography which makes fisheries and the consumption of seafood products extremely valuable. While Portugal captured 185,000 metric tons of fish in 2019, down from the 222,000 metric tons in 2010, fish and seafood represent the single highest import of biocapacity from abroad, amounting to 1,600,000 global hectares in total.<ref>{{cite journal|last1=Murthy |first1=Adeline |last2=Galli |first2=Alessandro |last3=Madeira |first3=Catarina |last4=Moreno Pires |first4=Sara |title= Consumer Attitudes towards Fish and Seafood in Portugal: Opportunities for Footprint Reduction|doi=10.3390/su15021363|publication-place=Basel|journal=Sustainability|year=2023|volume=15 |issue=2 |page=1363|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230123052257/https://mdpi-res.com/d_attachment/sustainability/sustainability-15-01363/article_deploy/sustainability-15-01363-v2.pdf?version=1673915949|archive-date=23 January 2023|url-status=live|eissn=2071-1050|access-date=17 April 2026|publisher=Multidisciplinary Digital Publishing Institute|url=https://www.mdpi.com/2071-1050/15/2/1363/pdf?version=1673915949|type=Article|doi-access=free |bibcode=2023Sust...15.1363M }}</ref>

=== Industry and services ===
{{main|Tourism in Portugal|:pt:Indústria automóvel em Portugal|l2 = Automotive industry in Portugal}}

[[File:Vehículos en el puerto de Setúbal, Portugal, 2019-05-24, DD 01.jpg|thumb|[[Volkswagen Autoeuropa]] cars in the Port of Setúbal]]

Portugal's industry accounts for 21.2% of the country's total GDP as of 2024, down from an annual average of 26% over the period between 1953 and 1973.<ref name="sectorsGDP" /><ref name="GDPgrowth">{{cite journal|journal=Economic Structures|doi=10.1186/s40008-024-00339-w|doi-access=free|title=Manufacturing production as a source of growth: the case of Portugal|first=Ricardo|last=Ferraz|publication-date=27 October 2024|publication-place=Berlin|publisher=Springer Berlin Heidelberg|issn=2193-2409|type=Research|volume=13|issue=1|page=4 |article-number=19 }}</ref> The lower contribution of manufacturing to Portugal's economy has led to lower real GDP growth rates between 1974 and 2019 than during the period between 1950 and 1973.<ref name="GDPgrowth" /> As of 2025, Portugal's automobile industry produced the biggest share of the country's exports.<ref name ="ExportsImports" /> The automobile industry accounts for 20.2% of the country manufacturing exports and 82.8% of the total value of its exports employing 43.247 workers in 2020.<ref>{{cite report|url=https://dgeconomia.gov.pt/gestao-de-ficheiros-externos-dgae-ano-2022/20220208_caderno_tematico_automovel_div29-pdf.aspx|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260501135303/https://dgeconomia.gov.pt/gestao-de-ficheiros-externos-dgae-ano-2022/20220208_caderno_tematico_automovel_div29-pdf.aspx|archive-date=1 May 2026|url-status=live|title=A Indústria Automóvel em Portugal|access-date=17 April 2026|language=pt-PT|trans-title=Automotive industry in Portugal|publication-place=Lisbon|publication-date=February 2022|author=Direção-Geral da Economia|publisher=self-published|page=4}}</ref>

Portugal's service sector accounted for 76.5% of the country's total economic output as of 2024.<ref name="sectorsGDP" /> Tourism, retail, and telecommunication are all major industries.<ref name="psi" /> Tourism is an important industry representing 11.4% of the Portugal's total GDP as of 2024.<ref>{{cite press release |author=Statistics Portugal|author-link=Instituto Nacional de Estatística (Portugal) |date= 1 August 2025|issn=2184-4534|title=Tourism satellite account – 2024|url=https://www.ine.pt/xportal/xmain?xpid=INE&xpgid=ine_destaques&DESTAQUESdest_boui=707093676&DESTAQUESmodo=2&xlang=en|location= Lisbon|publisher=self-published|access-date=1 May 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260501144007/https://www.ine.pt/ngt_server/attachfileu.jsp?look_parentBoui=740533348&att_display=n&att_download=y|archive-date=1 May 2026|url-status=live}}</ref> Portugal attracted 29 million international tourists in 2024,<ref>{{cite report|page=20|url=https://www.ine.pt/xportal/xmain?xpid=INE&xpgid=ine_publicacoes&PUBLICACOESpub_boui=66197834&PUBLICACOESmodo=2&xlang=en|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260210221313/https://www.ine.pt/ngt_server/attachfileu.jsp?look_parentBoui=736373015&att_display=n&att_download=y|archive-date=10 February 2026|url-status=live|title=Estatísticas do Turismo - 2024|language=pt-PT|issn=0377-2306|isbn=978-989-25-0722-4|publication-place=Lisbon|author=Statistics Portugal|author-link=Instituto Nacional de Estatística (Portugal)|publisher=self-published|access-date=1 May 2026|trans-title=Tourism Statistics - 2024|publication-date=9 July 2025}}</ref> [[World Tourism rankings|ranking fifteenth]] in the world in that year for inbound tourism.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Global and regional tourism performance |url=https://www.untourism.int/tourism-data/un-tourism-tourism-dashboard |access-date=1 May 2026|author=UN Tourism|publisher=self-published|publication-date=22 April 2026}}</ref>

=== Infrastructure ===
{{Main|Transport in Portugal|Energy in Portugal}}

[[File:Túnel do Marão.jpg|thumb|The {{ill|Marão Tunnel|pt|Túnel do Marão|lt=Marão Tunnel}} is the third-longest road tunnel on the [[Iberian Peninsula]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://servicos.infrastruturasdeportugal.pt/pt-pt/a-descobrir/obras-de-arte/tunel-do-marao-ips |title=Tunel do Marão |publisher=[[Infraestruturas de Portugal]]|date=May 2016 |access-date=16 January 2024}}</ref>]]

Portugal has a {{convert|14342|km|mi|0|abbr=on}} road network, of which {{convert|3113|km|mi|0|abbr=on}} are part of a [[Roads in Portugal#Motorways|system of 48 motorways]], making it the [[Evolution of motorway construction in European nations|8th largest motorway system among 42 European countries]] as of 2024.<ref>{{cite report|title=Estatísticas dos Transportes e Comunicações - 2024|issn=0377-2292|isbn=978-989-25-0723-1|author=Instituto Nacional de Estatística, I.P.|publisher=self-published|publication-place=Lisbon, Portugal|publication-date=November 2025|url=https://www.ine.pt/xurl/pub/761757686|access-date=17 April 2026|page=12}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/databrowser/view/ttr00002/default/table|doi=10.2908/TTR00002|doi-access=free|author=Eurostat|publisher=self-published|website=Eurostat|access-date=17 April 2026|title=Total length of motorways|date=16 April 2026}}</ref> The country has 37 civil airports,<ref>{{cite report|title=Estatísticas dos Transportes e Comunicações - 2024|issn=0377-2292|isbn=978-989-25-0723-1|author=Instituto Nacional de Estatística, I.P.|publisher=self-published|publication-place=Lisbon, Portugal|publication-date=November 2025|url=https://www.ine.pt/xurl/pub/761757686|access-date=24 April 2026|page=56}}</ref> of which five are international airports.{{efn|Three international airports are located on the mainland – [[Lisbon Airport|Lisbon]] ([[List of the busiest airports in Portugal|the busiest in the country]]), [[Porto Airport|Porto]], and [[Faro Airport|Faro]] airports – with [[Madeira Airport|Funchal]] airport on [[Madeira]], and [[John Paul II Ponta Delgada Airport|Ponta Delgada]] airport in the [[Azores]].<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.ana.pt/pt |title=10 Aeroportos em Portugal |publisher=ANA Aeroportos |access-date=9 December 2025 }}</ref>}} A national railway system is administered by [[Comboios de Portugal]] (CP).<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.cp.pt/info/pt/visao-missao-valores |title=Visão, Missão e Valores |publisher=CP - Comboios de Portugal |access-date=9 December 2025}}</ref> [[Rail transport]] of passengers and goods is made using the {{convert|2526|km|mi|0|abbr=on}} of railway lines in service as of 2024.<ref>{{cite report|title=Estatísticas dos Transportes e Comunicações - 2024|issn=0377-2292|isbn=978-989-25-0723-1|author=Instituto Nacional de Estatística, I.P.|publisher=self-published|publication-place=Lisbon, Portugal|publication-date=November 2025|url=https://www.ine.pt/xurl/pub/761757686|access-date=17 April 2026|page=11}}</ref> The major seaports are located in [[Port of Sines|Sines]], [[Leixões]], [[Port of Lisbon|Lisbon]], [[Setúbal]], [[Aveiro, Portugal|Aveiro]], [[Figueira da Foz]], and [[Faro, Portugal|Faro]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.ine.pt/xportal/xmain?xpid=INE&xpgid=ine_indicadores&indOcorrCod=0002571&contexto=bd&selTab=tab2&xlang=pt|title=Movimento de embarcações de comércio (N.º) por Porto declarante e Tipo de fluxo das embarcações; Mensal |access-date=9 December 2025|publisher=INE |date=24 September 2025 }}</ref>

As of 2023, 66.7% of Portugal's energy consumption was supplied from abroad, representing the eleventh-highest level of energy dependency in the European Union.<ref>{{cite report|isbn= 978-972-8646-87-5|publication-date=29 May 2025|publication-place=Lisbon|url=https://www.dgeg.gov.pt/media/b4fhd0lv/dgeg-aen-2025e.pdf|title=Energia em Números|edition=7th|publisher=Agência para a Energia|author1=Observatório da Energia|author2=Direção-Geral de Energia e Geologia - Direção de Serviços de Planeamento Energético e Estatística|author3=Agência para a Energia - Direção de Formação, Informação e Educação|access-date=4 May 2026|trans-title=Energy in Figures|language=pt-PT|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20250531061548/https://www.dgeg.gov.pt/media/b4fhd0lv/dgeg-aen-2025e.pdf|archive-date=31 May 2025|url-status=live|pages=44–46}}</ref> The country is pursuing [[Renewable energy in Portugal|energy transition]] and has invested in the development of renewable energy sources such as the [[Aguçadoura Wave Farm|world's first commercial wave power farm]].<ref>{{cite act|title=Resolução da Assembleia da República n.º 127/2025|url=https://files.diariodarepublica.pt/1s/2025/04/07100/0000600300.pdf|access-date=4 May 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20250421131045/https://files.diariodarepublica.pt/1s/2025/04/07100/0000600300.pdf|archive-date=21 April 2025|url-status =live|author=[[Assembly of the Republic (Portugal)|Assembly of the Republic]] |trans-title=Resolution of the Assembly of the Republic No. 127/2025 |at=No. 71/2025, Series 1|pinpoint=pp. 89-93|location={{lang|pt-PT|[[Diário da República]]}}|date=10 April 2025|language=pt-PT}}</ref><ref>{{cite journal |last1=Silva |first1=Dina |last2=Rusu |first2=Eugen |last3=Guedes Soares |first3=C. |title=The Effect of a Wave Energy Farm Protecting an Aquaculture Installation |journal=Energies |date=13 August 2018 |volume=11 |issue=8 |pages=2109 |doi=10.3390/en11082109 |doi-access=free }}</ref> Portugal has expanded the role of renewable sources in its energy sector, with renewables accounting for 35.2% of energy consumption, up from 21.9% in 2007, and 78.1% of [[Electricity generation|total installed capacity]], compared with 59.3% in 2014.<ref>{{cite report|isbn= 978-972-8646-87-5|publication-date=29 May 2025|publication-place=Lisbon|url=https://www.dgeg.gov.pt/media/b4fhd0lv/dgeg-aen-2025e.pdf|title=Energia em Números|edition=7th|publisher=Agência para a Energia|author1=Observatório da Energia|author2=Direção-Geral de Energia e Geologia - Direção de Serviços de Planeamento Energético e Estatística|author3=Agência para a Energia - Direção de Formação, Informação e Educação|access-date=4 May 2026|trans-title=Energy in Figures|language=pt-PT|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20250531061548/https://www.dgeg.gov.pt/media/b4fhd0lv/dgeg-aen-2025e.pdf|archive-date=31 May 2025|url-status=live|pages=44,53-54,76}}</ref> In 2021, the country completed the phase-out of coal-fired generation.<ref>{{cite journal |last1=Moreira |first1=Ricardo |title=A tale of two (un)Just Transitions: the end of the coal-fired power plants in Portugal |journal=Energy Policy |date=September 2025 |volume=204 |article-number=114658 |doi=10.1016/j.enpol.2025.114658 |doi-access=free |bibcode=2025EnPol.20414658M }}</ref>

== Demographics ==
{{Main|Demographics of Portugal}}

{{See also|Portuguese people}}

[[File:Puente de Don Luis I, Oporto, Portugal, 2019-06-02, DD 29-31 HDR.jpg|thumb|upright 1.2|[[Porto]] is the [[List of cities in Portugal|second largest city]] in Portugal, with its [[Porto Metropolitan Area|metropolitan area]] the country's second-largest.]]

Portugal has a population of 10,749,635, of whom 9,205,938 are Portuguese nationals and the remainder are foreign residents at 1,543,697, as of 2024.<ref name="populationPress">{{cite press release |author=Statistics Portugal|author-link=Instituto Nacional de Estatística (Portugal) |date= 18 June 2025|title=Estimates of resident population in Portugal 2024|url=https://www.ine.pt/xportal/xmain?DESTAQUESdest_boui=707078398&DESTAQUESmodo=2&&xpgid=ine_destaques&xpid=INE&xlang=en|location= Lisbon, Portugal|publisher=self-published|access-date=25 April 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260117075607/https://www.ine.pt/ngt_server/attachfileu.jsp?look_parentBoui=733217027&att_display=n&att_download=y|archive-date=17 January 2026|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{Cite report|title=Relatório de Migrações e Asilo 2024|trans-title=Report on Migrations and Asylum 2024|language=pt-PT|author=AIMA I.P. - DPEE – Direção de Planeamento, Estudos e Estatística|isbn=978-989-35625-8-1|date=October 2025|access-date=March 28, 2026|url=https://aima.gov.pt/media/pages/documents/fec4d6a712-1760603125/relatorio-migracoes-e-asilo-2024.pdf|page=2|edition=Digital}}</ref> Portugal is steadily aging and has the world's third-highest proportion of elderly citizens, comprising nearly one-fourth of its entire population.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Population ages 65 and above (% of total population)|url=https://data.worldbank.org/indicator/SP.POP.65UP.TO.ZS|access-date=25 April 2026 |author=World Bank|publisher=self-published|website=World Bank Open Data|archive-date=23 March 2026 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260323030148/https://data.worldbank.org/indicator/SP.POP.65UP.TO.ZS|url-status=live|publication-place=Washington, D.C.}}</ref> With a female share of the population at 52.2%, the country has the fourth-highest proportion of females in the European Union and one of the [[List of countries by sex ratio|world's highest]].<ref>{{cite book|isbn=978-972-597-449-0|author=Comissão para a Cidadania e a Igualdade de Género (CIG)|publisher=self-published|publication-date=23 December 2025|publication-place=Lisbon|url=https://www.cig.gov.pt/wp-content/uploads/2026/01/Boletim-2025_Versao-FINAL_dadoscorretos_site-1.pdf|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260305235653/https://www.cig.gov.pt/wp-content/uploads/2026/01/Boletim-2025_Versao-FINAL_dadoscorretos_site-1.pdf|archive-date=5 March 2026|url-status=live|title=Igualdade de género em Portugal: Boletim Estatístico 2025|access-date=25 April 2026|pages=16–17|language=pt-PT|trans-title=Gender Equality in Portugal: Statistical Bulletin 2025}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |title=Population, female (% of total population)|url=https://data.worldbank.org/indicator/SP.POP.TOTL.FE.ZS |access-date=25 April 2026 |author=World Bank|publisher=self-published|publication-place=Washington, D.C.|website=World Bank Open Data|archive-date=1 March 2026 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260301210058/https://data.worldbank.org/indicator/SP.POP.TOTL.FE.ZS|url-status=live}}</ref>

Portugal has a fertility rate of 1.4, which is below the [[Sub-replacement fertility|replacement rate]] of 2.1, is one of the [[List of countries by total fertility rate|world's lowest]].<ref name="populationPress" /> The country has had a fertility rate below the replacement rate of 2.1 since the 1980s that has led to the country having a [[Population pyramid|median age]] of 47.3, one of the [[List of countries by median age|highest in the world]].<ref>{{cite journal|doi=10.4054/DemRes.2004.S3.3|doi-access=free|publication-date=17 Apr 2004|article-number=3|type=Research article|journal=Demographic Research|title=Value Orientations and the Second Demographic Transition (SDT) in Northern, Western and Southern Europe: An Update|last1=Surkyn|last2=Lesthaeghe|first1=Johan|first2=Ron|issn=1435-9871|url=https://www.demographic-research.org/special/3/3/S3-3.pdf|publisher=Max Planck Institute for Demographic Research|publication-place=Rostock|access-date=25 April 2026|pages=45–86|volume=S3|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20060323042220/http://www.demographic-research.org/special/3/3/s3-3.pdf|archive-date=23 March 2006|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name="populationPress" /><ref>{{cite web|url=https://population.un.org/dataportal/data/indicators/67,49/locations/4,8,12,16,20,24,660,28,32,51,533,36,40,31,44,48,50,52,112,56,84,204,60,64,68,535,70,72,76,92,96,100,854,108,132,116,120,124,136,140,148,152,156,344,446,158,170,174,178,184,188,384,191,192,531,196,203,408,180,208,262,212,214,218,818,222,226,232,233,748,231,238,234,242,246,250,254,258,266,270,268,276,288,292,300,304,308,312,316,320,831,324,624,328,332,340,348,352,356,360,364,368,372,833,376,380,388,392,832,400,398,404,296,412,414,417,418,428,422,426,430,434,438,440,442,450,454,458,462,466,470,584,474,478,480,175,484,583,492,496,499,500,504,508,104,516,520,524,528,540,554,558,562,566,570,807,580,578,512,586,585,591,598,600,604,608,616,620,630,634,410,498,638,642,643,646,652,654,659,662,663,666,670,882,674,678,682,686,688,690,694,702,534,703,705,90,706,728,724,144,275,729,740,752,756,760,762,764,626,768,772,776,780,788,792,795,796,798,800,804,784,826,834,840,850,858,860,548,862,704,876,732,900,887,894,716/start/2024/end/2024/table/pivotbylocation?df=67e9fdb2-341a-4b63-8655-87fae18ae077|author=United Nations Population Division|publisher=United Nations|website=Population Division Data Portal|title=World Population Prospects: The 2024 Revision|access-date=1 May 2026|date=2024}}</ref> As of 2024, 24.3% of the population is aged 65 or older.<ref name="populationPress" /> Despite of the effects of net migration, due to low fertility rates Portugal's population is projected to drop to 8.3 million by 2100.<ref>{{cite press release |author=Statistics Portugal|author-link=Instituto Nacional de Estatística (Portugal) |date= 30 September 2025|title=Projections of resident population in Portugal 2025-2100|url=https://www.ine.pt/xportal/xmain?xpid=INE&xpgid=ine_destaques&DESTAQUESdest_boui=707257820&DESTAQUESmodo=2|location= Lisbon|publisher=self-published|access-date=25 April 2026|issn=2184-4534}}</ref>

Historically a country of emigration,<ref>{{cite book|title=Portugal: a country study|url=https://tile.loc.gov/storage-services/master/frd/frdcstdy/po/portugalcountrys00sols_0/portugalcountrys00sols_0.pdf|author= Federal Research Division, Library of Congress|publication-place= Washington D.C., United States|editor-last=Solsten|editor-first=Eric|series=Area handbook series|publication-date=January 1993|edition=2d|isbn=0-8444-0776-3|issn=1057-5294|access-date=25 April 2026 |chapter-url=http://countrystudies.us/portugal/48.htm|publisher=U.S. Government Printing Office|chapter=Emigration|department=Population|oclc=44354987|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110629081956/http://countrystudies.us/portugal/48.htm|archive-date=29 June 2011|url-status=live}}</ref> Portugal has been a net recipient of [[Immigration to Portugal|immigrants]] since 1993 except between 2011 and 2016 during the 
[[2010–2014 Portuguese financial crisis|Portuguese financial crisis]].<ref>{{cite book|isbn=972-673-728-1|title=30 anos de 25 de Abril: um retrato estatístico|url=https://www.ine.pt/ngt_server/attachfileu.jsp?look_parentBoui=267629&att_display=n&att_download=y|access-date=25 April 2026|publication-date=April 2004|publication-place=Lisbon|language=pt-PT|chapter=1. População e território|page=8|author-link=Instituto Nacional de Estatística (Portugal)|author=Statistics Portugal|publisher=self-published|trans-title=30 Years of 25 April: a statistical portrait|trans-chapter=1. Population and territory}}</ref><ref>{{cite journal|issn=2183-4385|title=Saldos migratórios, 2000-2017|language=pt-PT|journal=OEm Fact Sheets|issue=10|hdl=10071/20347|url=https://repositorio.iscte-iul.pt/bitstream/10071/20347/5/report_hdl20347.pdf|access-date=25 April 2026|pages=5,6|trans-title=Net migration, 2000-2017|first1=Rui Pena|last1=Pires|first2=Inês|last2=Vidigal|publisher=Observatório da Emigração|publication-date=March 2020|publication-place=Lisbon|archive-date=3 July 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200703032312/http://observatorioemigracao.pt/np4/file/7354/OEm_FactSheet_10_2020_Saldos.pdf|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name="populationPress" /> Since 2016, Portugal has experienced a marked increase in immigration, with the proportion of non-nationals in the total population rising from 3.5% to 9.8% by 2024, the largest concentrations living in the [[Algarve]] and the [[Lisbon metropolitan area]], and with 24.5% of all births registered in 2024 being to foreign-born women.<ref>{{cite web|author1=Eurostat |url=https://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/databrowser/bookmark/6b569dd8-b96c-4111-a727-8e49e1aad2c5?lang=en&createdAt=2026-04-25T18:59:34Z|title=Population on 1 January by age, sex and broad group of citizenship|doi=10.2908/MIGR_POP2CTZ|doi-access=free|publisher=[[Eurostat]]|access-date=25 April 2026|date=9 April 2026}}</ref><ref name="immigrationPress" /><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.ine.pt/xportal/xmain?xpid=INE&xpgid=ine_indicadores&indOcorrCod=0012437&contexto=bd&selTab=tab2&xlang=en|title=Statistics Portugal - Data Base - Indicator 0012437|author=Statistics Portugal|author-link=Instituto Nacional de Estatística (Portugal)|publisher=self-published|access-date=25 April 2026|date=29 April 2025}}</ref> In Portugal, White Portuguese constitute the largest [[Race (human categorization)|racial]] and [[Ethnicity|ethnic group]], representing 84.2% of the population, followed by multiracial Portuguese at 3.4%, [[Black Portuguese]] at 2.2%, [[Luso-Asians|Asian Portuguese]] at 0.7%, and the [[Romani people in Portugal|Romani]] at 0.6%.<ref name="immigrationPress" />

In 2023, 88% of the Portuguese population lived in urban areas.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.ine.pt/xportal/xmain?xpid=INE&xpgid=ine_indicadores&indOcorrCod=0008856&contexto=bd&selTab=tab2&xlang=en|title=Statistics Portugal - Data Base - Indicator 0008856|author=Statistics Portugal|author-link=Instituto Nacional de Estatística (Portugal)|publisher=self-published|access-date=25 April 2026|date=9 August 2024}}</ref> The capital city, [[Lisbon]], has a population of 575,739 as of 2024. It is part of [[Lisbon metropolitan area]], the biggest [[Metropolitan areas in Portugal|metropolitan area]] of Portugal with 3 million people.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.ine.pt/xportal/xmain?xpid=INE&xpgid=ine_indicadores&indOcorrCod=0012918&contexto=bd&selTab=tab2&xlang=en|title=Statistics Portugal - Data Base - Indicator 0012918|author=Statistics Portugal|author-link=Instituto Nacional de Estatística (Portugal)|publisher=self-published|access-date=25 April 2026|date=18 June 2025}}</ref>

=== Religion ===
<!-- If you want to expand this section, please add new info into the main article: "Religion in Portugal", your work there will be very appreciated. -->
{{Main|Religion in Portugal}}

{{Pie chart
| thumb = right
| caption = Religious affiliation in Portugal, according to the 2021 census:<ref name="Censos2021">{{cite web |url= https://tabulador.ine.pt/indicador/?id=0011644|title=Resident population with 15 and more years old (No.) by Place of residence at Census date [2021] (NUTS - 2013) and Religion; Decennial|type = article|website=Statistics Portugal - Official Web Portal|publisher=Statistics Portugal|author=INE|date=23 November 2022|access-date=25 February 2026}}</ref>
| label1 = [[Catholic Church|Catholicism]]
| value1 = 80.2
| color1 = #d4213d
| label2 = [[Protestantism]]
| value2 = 2.1
| color2 = DodgerBlue
| label3 = Other Christian
| value3 = 2.4
| color3 = Pink
| label4 = Other religion
| value4 = 1.13
| color4 = Gray
| label5 = [[Irreligious|No religion]]
| value5 = 14.1
| color5 = Honeydew
}}

Portugal is a [[secular state]] {{ill|Law on the separation of church and state (Portugal)|pt|Lei da Separação do Estado das Igrejas|lt=since 1911}},<ref>{{cite web|url=https://diariodarepublica.pt/dr/detalhe/decreto/92-1911-205606|website=Diário da República Eletrónico|title=Decreto, de 21 de abril|language=pt-PT|trans-title=Decree, of April 21|date=21 April 1911|access-date=March 2, 2026|publisher=Imprensa Nacional – Casa da Moeda, S. A.|location=Lisbon|author=Ministry of Justice}}</ref> and it guarantees [[religious freedom]].{{efn|[[Religious freedom]] was also reaffirmed by the 1940 Concordata (later amended in 1971) between Portugal and the [[Holy See]] and the 2001 Religious Freedom Act.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://arquivos.rtp.pt/conteudos/acordo-da-concordata-em-portugal/ |title=Acordo da Concordata em Portugal |publisher=RTP |date=9 February 2000 |access-date=7 December 2025 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://arquivos.rtp.pt/conteudos/revisao-da-concordata/ |title=Revisão da Concordata |publisher=RTP |date=6 January 2000 |access-date=7 December 2025 }}</ref>}} Although Portugal has no [[state religion|official religion]], the [[Catholic Church in Portugal|Catholic Church]] has a long history there that predates the country's formation and can be traced back to the 3rd century.<ref>{{cite journal|doi=10.5944/etfi.2.2009.1958|publication-date=30 April 2009|title=Sobre a cristianização da Lusitânia: novas reflexões a partir dos dados históricos e das evidências arqueológicas|issn=1131-7698|eissn=2340-1354|journal=Espacio Tiempo y Forma|series=Serie I (Nueva época), Prehistoria y Arqueología|pages=205–220|doi-access=free|url=https://revistas.uned.es/index.php/ETFI/article/view/1958/1834|type=Article|issue=2|publisher=Universidad Nacional de Educación a Distancia: Facultad de Geografía e Historia|publication-place=Madrid|first=André|last=Carneiro|access-date=27 April 2026|language=pt-PT|trans-title=On the Christianisation of Lusitania: new reflections based on historical data and archaeological evidence}}</ref> According to the 2021 Census, 80.2% of the Portuguese population are Catholic, while 14.7% are nonreligious.<ref name="Censos2021" />

The country has small [[Protestantism in Portugal|Protestant]], [[The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints in Portugal|Latter-day Saints]], [[Islam in Portugal|Muslim]], [[Hinduism in Portugal|Hindu]], [[Sikhism in Portugal|Sikh]], [[Eastern Orthodox Church]], {{ill|Jehovah's Witnesses in Portugal|pt|Testemunhas de Jeová em Portugal
|lt=Jehovah's Witnesses}}, [[Baháʼí Faith in Portugal|Baháʼí]], [[Buddhism in Portugal|Buddhist]], [[Judaism in Portugal|Jewish]], and [[Kardecist spiritism|Spiritist]] communities. Influences from [[African Traditional Religion]] and Chinese Traditional Religion are also felt among many people, particularly in fields related to Traditional Chinese Medicine and Traditional African Herbal Medicine.{{efn|Chinese medical science is well known in Portugal and is widely accepted by the people. Portugal is the first European Union country that specifically provided legislation for acupuncture and Chinese medical science.<ref>{{cite journal |last1=Song |first1=Haoyan |last2=Gao |first2=Jingran |last3=Jia |first3=Hao |title=Usage and promotion on Chinese medicine in Portuguese-speaking countries |journal=Pharmacological Research |date=June 2021 |volume=168 |article-number=105591 |doi=10.1016/j.phrs.2021.105591 |pmid=33813028 }}</ref>}} Even though Portugal has deep ties with Christianity, as of 2019<!--the year when the interviews were conducted--> the majority of its people were shown to be tolerant towards followers of other faiths, with the [[Islam in Portugal|Muslim community]] perceiving itself as thoroughly integrated into Portugal and believing that the country provided conditions conducive to smooth integration.<ref>{{cite journal |last1=de Carvalho |first1=Cátia Moreira |last2=Neyroud |first2=Peter |last3=Pinto |first3=Isabel R. |last4=Pinto |first4=Marta |title=The Portuguese Muslim community: integration and its role against radicalization |journal=Security Journal |date=March 2025 |volume=38 |issue=1 |article-number=17 |doi=10.1057/s41284-025-00464-6 |doi-access=free |hdl=10216/172256 |hdl-access=free }}</ref>

=== Languages ===

{{Main|Languages of Portugal}}

{{See also|Portuguese language}}

[[File:Genísio04.jpg|thumb|left|A sign in [[Mirandese language|Mirandese]] in [[Miranda do Douro]]|alt=Photograph of a white street sign mounted on a tan wall reads in Mirandese “Rue de L Cruzeiro” with “Rua do Cruzeiro” written in Portuguese below in script, and a small leaf logo at the top.]]

Portuguese is the official and predominantly spoken language in Portugal.<ref>{{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Fundamental principles |article= 11|clause=3|quote= The official language is Portuguese.|edition=7th|access-date = 17 April 2026}}</ref><ref>{{cite report |author=((European Commission Directorate-General for Education, Youth, Sport and Culture and Verian)) |title=Europeans and their languages |url=https://op.europa.eu/publication-detail/-/publication/1024ff67-8133-11ef-a67d-01aa75ed71a1 |year=2024 |page=11 |location=Luxembourg |publisher=[[Publications Office of the European Union]] |series=Special Eurobarometer|volume =540 |docket=NC-02-24-122-EN-N |isbn=978-92-68-12045-3 |issn=2811-9576 |doi=10.2766/28257 |doi-access=free |access-date=15 April 2026}}</ref> It is one of 24 official and working [[languages of the European Union]].<ref>{{CELEX|01958R0001-20130701|text=Regulation No 1 determining the languages to be used by the European Economic Community}}</ref> Portuguese is the fifth-most widely spoken first language in the world, with around 250 million native speakers.<ref>{{cite book|last1=Branco |first1=António |last2=Grilo |first2=Sara |last3=Silva |first3=João |doi=10.1007/978-3-031-28819-7_30|chapter=Language Report Portuguese|title=European Language Equality: A Strategic Agenda for Digital Language Equality|pages=195–198|publication-place=Cham|publisher=Springer|isbn=978-3-031-28819-7|publication-date=6 June 2023|doi-access=free|series=Cognitive Technologies|edition=1st}}</ref>

[[Portuguese Sign Language]] is officially protected by the country's Constitution.<ref>{{cite constitution |polity=Portugal |date=12 August 2005| url = https://www.parlamento.pt/sites/EN/Parliament/Documents/Constitution7th.pdf|part= Part I: Fundamental rights and duties, Title III: Economic, social and cultural rights and duties, Chapter III: Cultural rights and duties |article= 74|clause=2|quote=In implementing the education policy, the state is charged with: Protecting and developing Portuguese sign language, as an expression of culture and an instrument foraccess to education and equal opportunities;|edition=7th|access-date = 4 May 2026}}</ref> Recognized regional language and dialect are the [[Mirandese language|Mirandese]], spoken in [[Terra de Miranda]], and [[Barranquenho]], in [[Barrancos]].<ref>{{cite act |orig-section=Article 234|author=Assembleia da República|trans-title=Law No. 7/99 |at=No. 24/1999, Series 1-A|location={{lang|pt-PT|[[Diário da República]]}} |url=https://diariodarepublica.pt/dr/detalhe/lei/7-1999-182838|date=29 January 1999|language=pt-PT|title=Lei n.º 7/99 |access-date=4 May 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20231209142327/https://files.diariodarepublica.pt/1s/1999/01/024a00/05740574.pdf|archive-date=9 December 2023|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite act |orig-section=Article 234|author=Assembleia da República|trans-title=Law No. 97/2021 |at=No. 252/2021, Series 1 |location={{lang|pt-PT|[[Diário da República]]}} |url=https://diariodarepublica.pt/dr/detalhe/lei/97-2021-176800370|date=30 December 2021|language=pt-PT|title=Lei n.º 97/2021  |access-date=4 May 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211230091531/https://files.dre.pt/1s/2021/12/25200/0000300004.pdf|archive-date=30 December 2021|url-status=live}}</ref> Portuguese people are typically bilingual, with 67.5% speaking two languages, and rank among the world's most proficient non-native English speakers, with Portugal placed sixth globally for English proficiency in the 2025 [[EF English Proficiency Index]].<ref>{{cite press release |author=Statistics Portugal|author-link=Instituto Nacional de Estatística (Portugal) |date= 17 October 2023|title=Adult Education Survey – 2022|url=https://www.ine.pt/xportal/xmain?xpid=INE&xpgid=ine_destaques&DESTAQUESdest_boui=594906827&DESTAQUESmodo=2&xlang=en|location= Lisbon|publisher=self-published|access-date=4 May 2026|issn=2184-4534|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20250803185316/https://www.ine.pt/ngt_server/attachfileu.jsp?look_parentBoui=631822324&att_display=n&att_download=y|archive-date=3 August 2025|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name="EF EPI Ranking">{{Cite report|title=EF English Proficiency Index|year=2025 |url=https://www.ef.com/assetscdn/WIBIwq6RdJvcD9bc8RMd/cefcom-epi-site/reports/2025/ef-epi-2025-english.pdf|access-date=2026-04-09|page=9|publisher=[[EF Education First]]|edition=2025|url-status= live|archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20260218090753/https://www.ef.com/assetscdn/WIBIwq6RdJvcD9bc8RMd/cefcom-epi-site/reports/2025/ef-epi-2025-english.pdf|archive-date=2026-02-18}}</ref>

=== Education ===
<!-- If you want to expand this section, please add new info into the main articles: "Education in Portugal" and "Higher education in Portugal", your work there will be very appreciated. -->
{{Main|Education in Portugal}}

[[File:Coimbra BW 2018-10-06 10-11-56.jpg|thumb|The [[University of Coimbra]] in [[Coimbra]] is the first university in Portugal.]]

The educational system is divided into preschool (for those under age six), basic education (nine years, in three stages, compulsory), secondary education (three years, compulsory since 2010), and higher education (subdivided into university and [[polytechnic (Portugal)|polytechnic]] education). Universities are usually organised into [[faculty (division)|faculties]]. Institutes and schools are also common designations for autonomous subdivisions of [[List of universities and colleges in Portugal|Portuguese higher education institutions]].<ref>{{Cite web |title=Sistema português de Ensino Superior |url=https://www.ucp.pt/pt-pt/internacionalestudar-na-catolicacandidatos-internacionais/sistema-portugues-de-ensino-superior |access-date=7 December 2025 |website=Universidade Católica Portuguesa |language=pt }}</ref>

Portuguese universities have existed since 1290. The [[University of Coimbra]], the oldest Portuguese university,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.topuniversities.com/universities/university-coimbra|title=University of Coimbra|date=16 July 2015|website=Top Universities|access-date=16 March 2020|archive-date=7 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200307221441/https://www.topuniversities.com/universities/university-coimbra|url-status=live}}</ref> was first established in Lisbon before moving to [[Coimbra]]. Historically, within the scope of the Portuguese Empire, the Portuguese founded the oldest engineering school in the [[Americas]] (the ''[[Real Academia de Artilharia, Fortificação e Desenho]]'' of [[Rio de Janeiro]]) in 1792, as well as the oldest medical college in Asia (the ''[[Escola Médico-Cirúrgica de Goa|Escola Médico-Cirúrgica]]'' of [[Goa]]) in 1842. Presently, the largest university in Portugal is the [[University of Lisbon]].<ref>{{Cite web| title=Sobre Nós |url=https://www.ulisboa.pt/sobre-nos |access-date=6 December 2025 |website=Lisbon University |language=pt }}</ref>

The [[Bologna process]] has been adopted by Portuguese universities and polytechnical institutes in 2006. Higher education in state-run educational establishments is provided on a competitive basis, a system of ''[[numerus clausus]]'' is enforced through a national database on student admissions. However, every higher education institution offers also a number of additional vacant places through other admission processes for sportsmen, mature applicants (over 23 years old), [[international students]], foreign students from the [[Lusosphere]], degree owners from other institutions, students from other institutions ([[Transfer admissions in the United States|academic transfer]]), former students (readmission), and course change, which are subject to specific standards and regulations set by each institution or course department.<ref>{{Cite web| title=Processo de Bolonha |url=https://aquila.iseg.ulisboa.pt/aquila/unidade/SecLic/questoes-frequentes-(faqs)/processo-de-bolonha |access-date=6 December 2025 |website=Lisbon School of Economics & Management |language=pt }}</ref>

=== Health ===

{{Main|Health in Portugal|Healthcare in Portugal}}

[[File:Hospitais da Universidade de Coimbra - main entrance.JPG|thumb|The [[Centro Hospitalar e Universitário de Coimbra]] in [[Coimbra]] is the largest medical complex in Portugal.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://benchmarking-acss.min-saude.pt/MH_CapacidadeUtilizadaDashboard|author=Ministry of Health|author-link=Ministry of Health (Portugal)|publisher=self-published|publication-date=27 April 2026|access-date=8 May 2026|title=Monitorização Mensal Hospitais - Capacidade Utilizada|trans-title=Monthly Hospital Monitoring – Utilized Capacity|language=pt-PT}}</ref>]]

Portugal has a predominantly [[Universal health care|universal tax-funded health care]] system, called {{lang|pt-PT|{{ill|National Health Service (Portugal)|pt|Serviço Nacional de Saúde|lt=Serviço Nacional de Saúde}}}} (SNS), that operates alongside public-sector health insurance schemes called health subsystems funded mainly through employee and
employer contributions, as well as private voluntary health insurance.<ref>{{cite report|title=Portugal: Health System Summary, 2024|publication-place=Copenhagen|publisher=WHO Regional Office for Europe|publication-date=2025|url=https://iris.who.int/server/api/core/bitstreams/7f21852d-5d94-4735-8135-8909b8d8d431/content|access-date=8 May 2026|isbn=9789289014564|eissn=2958-9193|page=2|first1=Inês|last1=Fronteira|first2=Gonçalo Figueiredo|last2=Augusto|first3=Anna|last3= Maresso|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260508214546/https://iris.who.int/server/api/core/bitstreams/7f21852d-5d94-4735-8135-8909b8d8d431/content|archive-date=8 May 2026|url-status=live}}</ref> Primary and hospital care are provided by both public and private entities, with the private sector and complementing services offered by the SNS.<ref>{{cite report|title=Portugal: Health System Summary, 2024|publication-place=Copenhagen|publisher=WHO Regional Office for Europe|publication-date=2025|url=https://iris.who.int/server/api/core/bitstreams/7f21852d-5d94-4735-8135-8909b8d8d431/content|access-date=8 May 2026|isbn=9789289014564|eissn=2958-9193|page=3|first1=Inês|last1=Fronteira|first2=Gonçalo Figueiredo|last2=Augusto|first3=Anna|last3= Maresso|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260508214546/https://iris.who.int/server/api/core/bitstreams/7f21852d-5d94-4735-8135-8909b8d8d431/content|archive-date=8 May 2026|url-status=live}}</ref> In 2023, Portugal's health care was 38% privately funded and 62% government-funded, the 3rd lowest public share on health spending in the European Union.<ref>{{cite report|author1=OECD|author2=European Observatory on Health Systems and Policies|publication-place=Paris|title=Country Health Profile 2025: Portugal|series=State of Health in the EU|publisher=OECD Publishing|publication-date=11 December 2025|url=https://www.oecd.org/content/dam/oecd/en/publications/reports/2025/12/country-health-profile-2025-country-notes_7e72146d/portugal_6d4acb43/56041c8e-en.pdf|access-date=8 May 2026|page=7|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260508213353/https://www.oecd.org/content/dam/oecd/en/publications/reports/2025/12/country-health-profile-2025-country-notes_7e72146d/portugal_6d4acb43/56041c8e-en.pdf|archive-date=8 May 2026|url-status=live}}</ref> Portugal has among the highest levels of health inequity in the [[OECD]], driven by limited public spending, uneven distribution of services, low household income, long waiting times, and policy shortcomings.<ref>{{cite journal|trans-title=Equity in Access to Health Care in Portugal: What Do We Know?|journal=Acta Médica Portuguesa|volume=38|issue=2|doi=10.20344/amp.21668|doi-access=free|url=https://www.actamedicaportuguesa.com/revista/index.php/amp/article/view/21668/15569|title=Equidade no Acesso aos Cuidados de Saúde em Portugal: O que Sabemos?|publisher=Centro Editor Livreiro da Ordem dos Médicos|language=pt-PT|access-date=8 May 2026|publication-date=9 December 2024|publication-place=Lisbon|pages=104–111|first1=Joana|last1=Fernandes|first2=Cláudia|last2=Furtado|first3=João|last3=Pereira|pmid=39653036 |eissn=1646-0758|issn=0870-399X|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260508221421/https://www.actamedicaportuguesa.com/revista/index.php/amp/article/download/21668/15569/120580|archive-date=8 May 2026|url-status=live}}</ref>

Portugal [[List of countries by life expectancy|ranked 23rd]] in the world in 2024 in life expectancy with 85.4 years for women and 79.8 years for men, and it had an [[infant mortality rate]] of 2.7 deaths per {{Nts|1000}} [[Live birth (human)|live births]].<ref name="oecdHealth">{{cite report|author1=OECD|author2=European Observatory on Health Systems and Policies|publication-place=Paris|title=Country Health Profile 2025: Portugal|series=State of Health in the EU|publisher=OECD Publishing|publication-date=11 December 2025|url=https://www.oecd.org/content/dam/oecd/en/publications/reports/2025/12/country-health-profile-2025-country-notes_7e72146d/portugal_6d4acb43/56041c8e-en.pdf|access-date=8 May 2026|page=2|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260508213353/https://www.oecd.org/content/dam/oecd/en/publications/reports/2025/12/country-health-profile-2025-country-notes_7e72146d/portugal_6d4acb43/56041c8e-en.pdf|archive-date=8 May 2026|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite report|author=United Nations Inter-Agency Group for Child Mortality Estimation|title=Levels & trends in child mortality: report 2025: estimates|publication-place=New York City|page=94|url=https://data.unicef.org/resources/levels-and-trends-in-child-mortality-2025/|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260508230123/https://data.unicef.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/03/UNIGME-Child-Mortality-Report-2025.pdf|archive-date=8 May 2026|url-status=live|access-date=8 May 2026|publication-date=17 March 2026|publisher=UNICEF|isbn=978-92-806-5736-4|oclc=1584388386}}</ref> In 2022, the leading cause of death were cardiovascular diseases, at 25.4%.<ref name="oecdHealth" /> Portugal presents several adverse public-health indicators, including the 3rd lowest share of people reporting good health in the European Union, in 2024, at 54%, the highest alcohol consumption with {{convert|11.9|l|impgal usgal}} consumed per person, in 2020, and the highest share of adult population living a [[sedentary lifestyle]], in 2022, at 73%, a pattern reinforced by limited active-transport infrastructure and unsafe conditions for pedestrians and cyclists.<ref>{{cite report|doi=10.2766/356346|doi-access=free|author=European Commission: Directorate-General for Education, Youth, Sport and Culture|publication-date=26 September 2022|publisher=Publications Office of the European Union|title= Sport and physical activity: full report|isbn=978-92-76-56432-4|docket=NC-09-22-460-EN-N|page=9|url=https://www.sportesalute.eu/images/studi-e-dati-dello-sport/schede/2022/98-Sport_physical_activity_2022_report.pdf|access-date=9 May 2026|publication-place=Luxembourg|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20250207090209/https://webgate.ec.europa.eu/ebsm/api/public/deliverable/download?doc=true&deliverableId=83654|archive-date=7 February 2025|url-status=live|oclc=1347440217}}</ref><ref>{{cite report|author1=OECD|author2=European Observatory on Health Systems and Policies|publication-place=Paris|title=Country Health Profile 2025: Portugal|series=State of Health in the EU|publisher=OECD Publishing|publication-date=11 December 2025|url=https://www.oecd.org/content/dam/oecd/en/publications/reports/2025/12/country-health-profile-2025-country-notes_7e72146d/portugal_6d4acb43/56041c8e-en.pdf|access-date=8 May 2026|pages=2-3,5-6|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260508213353/https://www.oecd.org/content/dam/oecd/en/publications/reports/2025/12/country-health-profile-2025-country-notes_7e72146d/portugal_6d4acb43/56041c8e-en.pdf|archive-date=8 May 2026|url-status=live}}</ref>

== Culture ==
{{Main|Culture of Portugal|Mass media in Portugal}}

[[File:Feira de Barcelos (05Set) 040.jpg|thumb|250px|upright|The [[Rooster of Barcelos|Barcelos Cockerel]] is a common symbol of Portugal|alt=Photograph of a market stall displaying many brightly painted Barcelos Cockerels with oversized red crests, black bodies, blue bases, and colourful heart-and-dot patterns, arranged closely together on tables.]]

Portugal has developed a specific culture due to, initially before its existence, the influence from various civilisations that have crossed Europe, especially the Mediterranean, and later, during the period of [[Portugal in the Age of Discovery|Portugal's engagement in the Age of Discovery]] which [[Colombian exchange|introduced cultural elements from outside of the European continent]] and became a central element of Portuguese national identity.<ref>{{multiref2
|1={{cite journal|title=Aspetos importantes do legado árabe na língua portuguesa|doi=10.34913/journals/lingualugar.2020.e418|last=Suisse|first=Abdelilah|journal=Língua-lugar: Literatura, História, Estudos Culturais|publisher=[[University of Geneva]]|publication-place=Geneva|eissn=2673-5091|publication-date=26 February 2026|pages=42–59|volume=1|issue=2|url=https://oap.unige.ch/journals/lingua-lugar/article/view/418/319|access-date=1 May 2026|language=pt-PT|trans-title=Important aspects of the Arab legacy in the Portuguese language|doi-access=free|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260501171132/https://access.archive-ouverte.unige.ch/access/metadata/99a2524e-2864-4a0e-86de-a9b8e0bb7bbf/download|archive-date=1 May 2026|url-status=live}}
|2={{cite book|page=124|publisher=University of Chicago Press|publication-place=Chicago, Illinois|lccn=2009017508|title=Colonial encounters in ancient Iberia: Phoenician, Greek, and indigenous relations|isbn=9780226148472|chapter=Chapter 4: Phoenician Colonization on the Atlantic Coast of the Iberian Peninsula|first=Ana Margarida|last=Arruda|editor-last1= Dietler|editor-first1=Michael|editor-last2=López-Ruiz|editor-first2=Carolina|publication-date=15 October 2009|oclc=593325476}}}}</ref><ref>{{cite journal|doi=10.1080/1070289X.2001.9962708|title=Remembering Vasco da Gama: Contested histories and the cultural politics of contemporary nation-building in Lisbon, Portugal|last=Sieby|first=R. Timothy|journal=Identities: Global Studies in Culture and Power|volume=8|issue=4|publication-date=1 December 2001|issn=1070-289X|eissn=1547-3384|pages=549–581|publisher=Taylor & Francis|publication-place=London}}</ref>

Portugal is well known for its [[Architecture of Portugal|heritage and architecture]], [[Sanctuary of Fátima|sacred sites]], [[List of festivals in Portugal|summer festivals]], [[Portuguese poetry|poetry]], its music (especially the [[fado]]), and [[Portuguese cuisine|cuisine]] (especially its [[Portuguese wine|wine]]).<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.visitportugal.com/en/node/231670|access-date=12 April 2026|website=www.visitportugal.com|title=Portugal's Top 10 Cultural Features|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20251114175510/https://www.visitportugal.com/en/node/231670|archive-date=14 November 2025}}</ref> As of 2026, [[UNESCO]] inscribed [[List of World Heritage Sites in Portugal|17 properties in Portugal on the World Heritage List]].<ref>{{cite web|title=World Heritage - List|url=https://www.unesco.org/en/world-heritage/list|website=UNESCO : Building Peace through Education, Science and Culture, communication and information|access-date=26 February 2026|url-status= live|archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20260206124451/https://www.unesco.org/en/world-heritage/list|archive-date= 6 February 2026}}</ref> There are [[Public holidays in Portugal|13 public holidays in Portugal]];<ref>{{cite act |author=Assembleia da República |trans-title=Law No. 7/2009 |at=No. 30/2009, Series 1|location={{lang|pt-PT|[[Diário da República]]}} |url=https://diariodarepublica.pt/dr/legislacao-consolidada/lei/2009-34546475|date=2 February 2009|language=pt-PT|title=Lei n.º 7/2009|access-date=1 May 2026 }}</ref> 10 June is the [[national day]] of Portugal, celebrated as the {{lang|pt-PT|Dia de Portugal, de Camões e das Comunidades Portuguesas}} ([[Portugal Day|Portugal, Camões, and Portuguese Communities Day]]).<ref>{{cite act |author=Presidency of the Council of Ministers|author-link=Council of Ministers (Portugal) |trans-title=Decree-Law No. 20-A/2016 |at=No. 81/2016, 1st Supplement, Series 1|location={{lang|pt-PT|[[Diário da República]]}} |url=https://diariodarepublica.pt/dr/detalhe/decreto-lei/20-a-2016-74277002|date=27 April 2016|language=pt-PT|title=Decreto-Lei n.º 20-A/2016|access-date=1 May 2026 }}</ref>

=== Art and architecture===
{{main|Portuguese art|Architecture of Portugal}}

{{multiple image
| alt2              = Photograph of Belém Tower standing at the water's edge under a cloudy sky, with ornate turrets, carved windows, and a narrow walkway where several people are walking.
