The history of visual art in Portugal dates back into the [[Art of the Upper Paleolithic|Paleolithic]]. The earliest evidence showing an attempt at depicting motion was found at the [[Prehistoric Rock Art Sites in the Côa Valley and Siega Verde]].<ref>{{cite report|author=International Council on Monuments and Sites|author-link=International Council on Monuments and Sites|url=https://publ.icomos.org/publicomos/jlbSai?html=Bur&base=technica&ref=44476&file=3548.pdf&path=1998_ICOMOS_Evaluation%20Volume_EN.pdf|series=ICOMOS Evaluation Volumes|publication-date=1 October 1998|access-date=12 April 2026|publication-place=Paris|title=Evaluation report of cultural properties - 1998|id=44476|page=46|publisher=self-published|via=PUBLICOMOS|type=Evaluation report|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260501200053/https://publ.icomos.org/publicomos/jlbSai?html=Bur&base=technica&ref=44476&file=3548.pdf&path=1998_ICOMOS_Evaluation%20Volume_EN.pdf|archive-date=1 May 2026|url-status=live}}</ref> Over time, foreign and native influences, together with developments in manufacturing, have led to the creation and development of a number of crafts that are typical of Portugal, the most notable of which being the {{lang|pt|[[azulejo]]}}, {{lang|pt|[[Gilded woodcarving in Portugal|talha dourada]]}}, and [[Portuguese pavement]],<ref>{{cite journal |last1=Sandu |first1=Irina Crina Anca |last2=Murta |first2=Elsa |last3=Neves |first3=Eva Raquel |last4=Pereira |first4=Manuel |last5=Sandu |first5=Andrei Victor |last6=Kuckova |first6=Stepanka |last7=Maurício |first7=António |title=A comparative interdisciplinary study of gilding techniques and materials in two Portuguese Baroque 'talha dourada' complexes |journal=Estudos de Conservação e Restauro |date=27 December 2016 |issue=4 |pages=47–71 Páginas |doi=10.34618/ecr.4.3080 |doi-access=free }}</ref><ref>{{cite book|last1=Resende |first1=Nuno |hdl=10216/147694|hdl-access=free|chapter=A arte da talha em madeira em Portugal: novas perspectivas|publisher=CITCEM -Centro de Investigação Transdisciplinar Cultura, Espaço e Memória|chapter-url=https://ler.letras.up.pt/uploads/ficheiros/19629.pdf|url=https://ler.letras.up.pt/uploads/ficheiros/19618.pdf|isbn=978-989-9082-51-9|series=Suportes do Património|volume=1|title= Madeira |publication-date=2022|publication-place=Porto|access-date=1 May 2026|archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20240706232939/https://ler.letras.up.pt/uploads/ficheiros/19618.pdf|archive-date=6 July 2024|url-status=live|language=pt-PT|trans-chapter=The art of wood carving in Portugal: new perspectives|trans-title=Wood|pages=206–227}}</ref><ref>{{cite journal |last1=Pereira |first1=Sílvia R.M. |last2=Conte |first2=Gloria |last3=Esteves |first3=Lurdes |last4=Pais |first4=Alexandre N. |last5=Mimoso |first5=João M. |title=Evolution of azulejo glaze technology in Portugal from the 16th to the onset of the 19th century |journal=Journal of the European Ceramic Society |date=July 2023 |volume=43 |issue=8 |pages=3804–3815 |doi=10.1016/j.jeurceramsoc.2023.01.038 }}</ref> which formed the basis of some Portuguese architectural styles, such as the [[Pombaline style]].{{cn|date=May 2026}}

Historically, religion, specifically Christianity, had an influential role in Portuguese art, as it was a recurrent theme widely employed in many art forms, such as in painting.<ref name="stVincentP" /> Throughout the country's history, artwork in Portugal was typically done by local artists who, depending on location, followed different variations in style, giving Portugal a diverse array of artistic styles throughout the country, an example of this being the {{ill|Typical thatch houses of Santana|pt|Casas típicas de Santana|lt=thatch houses of Santana}}, in [[Madeira]].<ref>{{cite journal|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20241221105821/https://mdpi-res.com/d_attachment/religions/religions-15-01563/article_deploy/religions-15-01563.pdf?version=1734774646|archive-date=21 December 2024|url-status=live|last1=Silva |first1=Fátima Matos |last2=Da Silva |first2=Carlos Gouveia |doi=10.3390/rel15121563|journal=Religions|title=The Baroque Religious Architecture of Paredes de Coura, Portugal, and the Transformation of the Territory|url=https://www.mdpi.com/2077-1444/15/12/1563/pdf?version=1734774646|access-date=13 April 2026|publisher=Multidisciplinary Digital Publishing Institute|volume=15|publication-place=Basel|issue=12|issn=2077-1444|publication-date=21 December 2024|pages=1–14|article-number=1563 |doi-access=free }}</ref>

=== Literature ===
{{Main|Portuguese literature}}

[[File:Camões, por Fernão Gomes.jpg|thumb|alt=A sepia-toned portrait drawing of Luís Vaz de Camões in ornate clothing with a large ruffled collar, shown from the chest up against a background with partially visible lettering saying "LVIS DE CAMÕES".|upright|left|[[Luís Vaz de Camões]], legendary poet of the [[Portuguese Renaissance]]]]

Portugal has a literary tradition that predates the [[Portuguese language]] going back into the early 13th century.<ref>{{cite book|editor-first1=Stephen|editor-last1=Parkinson|editor-first2=Cláudia|editor-last2=Pazos Alonso|editor-first3=T. F.|editor-last3=Earle|publisher=Tamesis|publication-place=Boydell & Brewer|title=A Companion to Portuguese Literature|chapter=Chapter 2: The Medieval Galician-Portuguese Lyric|pages=37–43|isbn=978-184-6157-08-0|oclc=1389178173|publication-date=19 November 2009|series=Monografías A|volume=282|first1=Rip|last1=Cohen|first2=
Stephen|last2=Parkinson|doi=10.1017/9781846157080.003|via=Cambridge Core}}</ref> Portuguese literature developed through song as well as the written page known as {{lang|pt-PT|[[cantigas]]}}.<ref name="cantigas">{{cite thesis|pages=43–46|publication-date=July 2010|degree=Master|hdl=10362/5503|first=Vera Mónica Lopes Inácio|last=Cordeniz|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260502011528/https://run.unl.pt/server/api/core/bitstreams/7f0885ab-148d-4032-b626-83645ac257db/content|archive-date=2 May 2026|url-status = live|title=As cantigas medievais Galeco-Portuguesas do repertório para canto acompanhado no séc. XX|hdl-access=free|trans-title=The medieval Galician-Portuguese songs from the accompanied singing repertoire in the 20th century|language=pt-PT|access-date=18 April 2026|publisher=School of Social and Human Sciences of the NOVA University of Lisbon|publication-place=Lisbon, Portugal|url=https://run.unl.pt/bitstreams/7f0885ab-148d-4032-b626-83645ac257db/download}}</ref> The {{lang|pt-PT|cantigas}} drew practitioners from all social ranging from King [[Denis of Portugal|Denis I]] to [[Martin Codax]] who was a [[minstrel]].<ref name="literatureHistory">{{cite book|editor-first1=Stephen|editor-last1=Parkinson|editor-first2=Cláudia|editor-last2=Pazos Alonso|editor-first3=T. F.|editor-last3=Earle|publisher=Tamesis|publication-place=Boydell & Brewer|title=A Companion to Portuguese Literature|chapter=Chapter 1: Eight Centuries of Portuguese Literature: An Overview|page=2|isbn=978-184-6157-08-0|oclc=1389178173|publication-date=19 November 2009|series=Monografías A|volume=282|first1=Helder|last1=Macedo|doi=10.1017/9781846157080.002|via=Cambridge Core}}</ref> The earliest work of Portugal's literature is the ''Ora faz ost’o senhor de Navarra'', a {{lang|pt-PT|[[Cantigas de escárnio e maldizer|cantiga de escárnio e maldizer]]}} written in [[Galician–Portuguese]] by [[João Soares de Paiva]] at around the year 1200.<ref name="cantigas" />

Portuguese literature developed under the influence of both European geopolitical developments and broader European literary traditions. The [[Hundred Years' War]] helped foster the development of Portuguese [[chronicle]]s by [[Fernão Lopes]], which constitute a valuable record of some of Europe's earliest encounters with peoples beyond the continent.<ref>{{cite book|doi=10.1017/9781846157080.002|editor-first1=Stephen|editor-last1=Parkinson|editor-first2=Cláudia|editor-last2=Pazos Alonso|editor-first3=T. F.|editor-last3=Earle|publisher=Tamesis|publication-place=Boydell & Brewer|title=A Companion to Portuguese Literature|chapter=Chapter 1: Eight Centuries of Portuguese Literature: An Overview|pages=2–5|isbn=978-184-6157-08-0|oclc=1389178173|publication-date=19 November 2009|series=Monografías A|volume=282|first1=Helder|last1=Macedo|via=Cambridge Core}}</ref><ref>{{cite book|editor-first1=Stephen|editor-last1=Parkinson|editor-first2=Cláudia|editor-last2=Pazos Alonso|editor-first3=T. F.|editor-last3=Earle|publisher=Tamesis|publication-place=Boydell & Brewer|title=A Companion to Portuguese Literature|chapter=Chapter 3: Fernão Lopes and Portuguese Prose Writing of the Middle Ages|pages=45–51|isbn=978-184-6157-08-0|oclc=1389178173|publication-date=19 November 2009|series=Monografías A|volume=282|first1=Stephen|last1=Parkinson|doi=10.1017/9781846157080.004|via=Cambridge Core}}</ref> European medieval chivalric literature, together with didactic religious literature transmitted through adaptations and partial translations, contributed to the development of [[Portuguese poetry]] in the translated works of [[Norman French]] [[List of Arthurian literature|Arturian narratives]].<ref name="literatureHistory" /><ref>{{cite book|editor-first1=Stephen|editor-last1=Parkinson|editor-first2=Cláudia|editor-last2=Pazos Alonso|editor-first3=T. F.|editor-last3=Earle|publisher=Tamesis|publication-place=Boydell & Brewer|title=A Companion to Portuguese Literature|chapter=Chapter 3: Fernão Lopes and Portuguese Prose Writing of the Middle Ages|pages=53–54|isbn=978-184-6157-08-0|oclc=1389178173|publication-date=19 November 2009|series=Monografías A|volume=282|first1=Stephen|last1=Parkinson|doi=10.1017/9781846157080.004|via=Cambridge Core}}</ref> Portuguese literature flourished during the [[Age of Discovery]], its most notable example being {{lang|pt-PT|[[Os Lusíadas]]}} by [[Luís Vaz de Camões]].<ref>{{cite book|editor-first1=Stephen|editor-last1=Parkinson|editor-first2=Cláudia|editor-last2=Pazos Alonso|editor-first3=T. F.|editor-last3=Earle|publisher=Tamesis|publication-place=Boydell & Brewer|title=A Companion to Portuguese Literature|chapter=Chapter 5: The Lusiads and the Literature of Portuguese Overseas Expansion|pages=72–83|isbn=978-184-6157-08-0|oclc=1389178173|publication-date=19 November 2009|series=Monografías A|volume=282|first1=Clive|last1=Willis|doi=10.1017/9781846157080.006|via=Cambridge Core}}</ref><ref>{{cite book|editor-first1=Stephen|editor-last1=Parkinson|editor-first2=Cláudia|editor-last2=Pazos Alonso|editor-first3=T. F.|editor-last3=Earle|publisher=Tamesis|publication-place=Boydell & Brewer|title=A Companion to Portuguese Literature|chapter=Chapter 4: Portuguese Theatre in the Sixteenth Century: Gil Vicente and António Ferreira|page=68|isbn=978-184-6157-08-0|oclc=1389178173|publication-date=19 November 2009|series=Monografías A|volume=282|first1=
Juliet|last1=Perkins|first2=T. F.|last2=Earle|doi=10.1017/9781846157080.005|via=Cambridge Core}}</ref> Modern Portuguese literature took shape through the work of [[Almeida Garrett]], one of the early founders of Portuguese Romanticism.<ref>{{cite book|editor-first1=Stephen|editor-last1=Parkinson|editor-first2=Cláudia|editor-last2=Pazos Alonso|editor-first3=T. F.|editor-last3=Earle|publisher=Tamesis|publication-place=Boydell & Brewer|title=A Companion to Portuguese Literature|chapter=Chapter 9: Almeida Garrett: Founder of Modern Portuguese Literature|pages=109–111|isbn=978-184-6157-08-0|oclc=1389178173|publication-date=19 November 2009|series=Monografías A|volume=282|first1=
Helena|last1=Carvalhão Buescu|doi=10.1017/9781846157080.010|via=Cambridge Core}}</ref> Portugal has one [[Nobel Prize in Literature|Nobel Prize&ndash;winning author]]&mdash;[[José Saramago]] (1998).<ref>{{cite web|title=The Nobel Prize in Literature 1998 - NobelPrize.org|url=https://www.nobelprize.org/prizes/literature/1998/summary/|access-date=27 December 2025|author=Nobel Prize Outreach|publication-date=2026|publisher=self-published|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260424120342/https://www.nobelprize.org/prizes/literature/1998/summary/|archive-date=24 April 2026|url-status=live}}</ref>

=== Music ===
{{Main|Music of Portugal}}

{{CSS image crop
|alt=Black-and-white photograph of Amália Rodrigues singing into a standing microphone, wearing a long dark gown and shawl, with one hand raised in expression and a guitarist partly visible in the background.
|Image = Amalia Rodrigues, Bestanddeelnr 922-1813 (cropped).jpg
|bSize = 280
|cWidth = 190
|cHeight = 200
|oTop = 40
|oLeft = 45
|Location = right
|Description = [[Amália Rodrigues]] was known as the "Queen of Fado"<ref>{{cite web|title=Projeto de Voto de Saudação n.º 370/XVI|url=https://app.parlamento.pt/webutils/docs/doc.pdf?path=6148523063484d364c793968636d356c6443397a6158526c63793959566b6c4d5a5763765247396a6457316c626e52766330466a64476c32615752685a47565159584a735957316c626e5268636938775a544e684d6d49304f43316a4e7a67354c54526c595449745954426a4d433032593251334e6a6c6c5a5751334d7a4d755a47396a65413d3d&fich=0e3a2b48-c789-4ea2-a0c0-6cd769eed733.docx&Inline=true|trans-title=Motion of Tribute No. 370/XVI|language=pt-PT|first=José Pedro |last=Aguiar-Branco|author-link=José Pedro Aguiar-Branco|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260503164016/https://app.parlamento.pt/webutils/docs/doc.pdf?path=6148523063484d364c793968636d356c6443397a6158526c63793959566b6c4d5a5763765247396a6457316c626e52766330466a64476c32615752685a47565159584a735957316c626e5268636938775a544e684d6d49304f43316a4e7a67354c54526c595449745954426a4d433032593251334e6a6c6c5a5751334d7a4d755a47396a65413d3d&fich=0e3a2b48-c789-4ea2-a0c0-6cd769eed733.docx&Inline=true|archive-date=3 May 2026|url-status=live|publisher=[[Assembly of the Republic (Portugal)|Assembleia da República]]|publication-place=Lisbon|publication-date=6 October 2024|access-date=14 April 2026}}</ref>
}}

The [[Music history of Portugal|history of music in Portugal]] dates back to the 6th century. The earliest record of a singer in Portugal is from the year 525.<ref>{{cite journal|page=171|url=https://rpm-ns.pt/index.php/rpm/article/view/148/154|publication-date=20 December 2014|publisher= Sociedade Portuguesa de Investigação em Música|issn=2183-8410|doi=10.57885/rpmns.148|first=Manuel Pedro|last=Ferreira|publication-place=Lisbon|journal=Portuguese Journal of Musicology|title= Da música na história de Portugal
|trans-title=On the Music in the History of Portugal|volume=4/5|issue=Revista Portuguesa de Musicologia, v. 4/5 (1994-1995) |language=pt-PT|access-date=14 April 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260426170530/https://rpm-ns.pt/index.php/rpm/article/download/148/154/396|archive-date=26 April 2026|doi-access=free|url-status=live}}</ref> Portuguese music initially consisted mostly of [[liturgical music]] and [[Galician-Portuguese lyric|troubadourism]].<ref>{{cite journal|pages=170–178|url=https://rpm-ns.pt/index.php/rpm/article/view/148/154|publication-date=20 December 2014|publisher= Sociedade Portuguesa de Investigação em Música|issn=2183-8410|doi=10.57885/rpmns.148|first=Manuel Pedro|last=Ferreira|publication-place=Lisbon|journal=Portuguese Journal of Musicology|title= Da música na história de Portugal
|trans-title=On the Music in the History of Portugal|volume=4/5|issue=Revista Portuguesa de Musicologia, v. 4/5 (1994-1995) |language=pt-PT|access-date=14 April 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260426170530/https://rpm-ns.pt/index.php/rpm/article/download/148/154/396|archive-date=26 April 2026|doi-access=free|url-status=live}}</ref> Over time, new folk traditions together with the influence of foreign cultures and the creation of new instruments, especially {{ill|Portuguese guitars|pt|Violas portuguesas|lt=guitars}}, led to a diverse variety of regional folk music such as the [[fado]], the [[Coimbra fado]], [[Desgarrada]], and [[Music of Madeira|Madeira's folk music]].<ref>{{cite journal|journal=The Musical Quarterly|volume=20|issue=4|title=The Folk-Music of Eastern Portugal|pages=96–106|jstor=738712|last=Gallop|first=Rodney|publication-date=October 1934|eissn=1741-8399|issn=0027-4631|publisher=[[G. Schirmer]]|publication-place=New York City}}</ref><ref>{{cite journal|pages=343–354|last=Gallop|first=R. A.|title=The Folk Music of Portugal: II.|jstor=728824|journal=Music and Letters|volume=14|issue=4|issn=0027-4224|eissn=1477-4631|publication-place=London|publication-date=October 1933|publisher=Oxford University Press}}</ref><ref>{{cite journal|url=https://www.e-publicacoes.uerj.br/contemporanea/article/view/3386/2954|publication-place=Rio de Janeiro|title=O fado de Portugal, do Brasil e do mundo: uma revisão das teorias sobre sua origem|trans-title=The fado of Portugal, Brazil and world: the theories about its origin|doi=10.12957/contemporanea.2012.3386|doi-access=free|language=pt-BR|journal=Revista Contemporânea|eissn=1806-0498|edition=20|volume=10|issue=2|publication-date=1 November 2012|pages=58–70|first=Ricardo|last= Nicolay|doi-broken-date=9 May 2026 |access-date=3 May 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260503174023/https://www.e-publicacoes.uerj.br/contemporanea/article/download/3386/2954/16169|archive-date=3 May 2026|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite book| editor-last = Wilson| editor-first = Thomas M.| title = Europe: An Encyclopedia of Culture and Society| publisher= Bloomsbury Academic| publication-date= 30 November 2023|isbn = 978-1-4408-5545-0| url         =https://books.google.com/books?id=pQjcEAAAQBAJ| access-date = 14 April 2026|volume=2|page=739|via=Google Books|publication-place=New York City|lccn=2022059195|oclc=1474125252}}</ref>

Popular music in Portugal after the [[Carnation Revolution]] has been heavily influenced by American trends, which has led into the evolution of [[Hip-hop tuga]] and popularization of [[Rock music in Portugal|Rock]].<ref>{{cite journal|title=Transatlantic Musical Flows in the Lusophone World: An Introduction|jstor=24318146|volume=2|issue=2|pages=7–24|last=Alge|first=Barbara|journal=The World of Music|issn=0043-8774|publisher=VWB - Verlag für Wissenschaft und Bildung|publication-date=2013|publication-place=Berlin}}</ref> Historically, Portugal has been a country of [[emigration]] which has heavily influenced the [[Pimba]] in the 20th century and led to the introduction of Portuguese music into other cultures such as the [[ukelele]] in [[Music of Hawaii|Hawaii]] in the 19th century.<ref>{{cite book|first=Richard |last=Elliott|title=Fado and the Place of Longing: Loss, Memory and the City|chapter-url-access=limited|chapter-url=https://books.google.com/books?id=Sa-gR-P-pVEC&q=pimba+music&pg=PA135|year=2010|publisher=Ashgate|page=135|chapter=Chapter 4: New Citizens of the Fadista world|isbn=9780754667957|via =Google Books|access-date=3 May 2026|lccn=2009046525|oclc=463675847|publication-place=Farnham|series=Ashgate popular and folk music series}}</ref><ref>{{cite book|last = Nidel| first = Richard O.| title = World Music: The Basics| publisher = Routledge| year = 2004|page =312| isbn = 978-0-415-96800-3| url = https://archive.org/details/worldmusic00rich_0|access-date=14 April 2026|publication-place=New York City|via=Wayback Machine|url-access=registration|lccn=2004019817|oclc=56355805}}</ref>

=== Holidays ===
{{Main|Public holidays in Portugal}}

[[File:Entrudo de Vila Boa de Ousilhão 26.jpg|thumb|A group of people celebrate the {{ill|Entrudo|pt|Entrudo|lt=Entrudo}}, in [[Vinhais]]]]

Officially, Portugal has 13 national, government-recognised holidays. Public holidays in Portugal are regulated by the {{ill|Portuguese Labour Code|pt|Código do Trabalho|lt=Labour Code}}.<ref name="Labour Code IX.234">{{cite act |orig-section=Article 234|author=Assembleia da República|trans-title=Law No. 7/2009 |at=No. 30/2009, Series 1|location={{lang|pt-PT|[[Diário da República]]}} |url=https://www.pgdlisboa.pt/leis/lei_mostra_articulado.php?artigo_id=1047A0234&nid=1047&tabela=leis&pagina=1&ficha=1&so_miolo=&nversao=#artigo|date=12 February 2009|language=pt-PT|title=Lei n.º 7/2009|access-date=3 May 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210920135006/https://www.pgdlisboa.pt/leis/lei_mostra_articulado.php?artigo_id=1047A0234&nid=1047&tabela=leis&pagina=1&ficha=1&so_miolo=&nversao=#artigo|archive-date=20 September 2021|url-status=live}}</ref> Besides the national holidays, there are 3 regional holidays celebrated only in [[Madeira]] and the [[Azores]] and 2 facultative holidays. The national holidays in Portugal are: [[New Year's Day]] on January 1, [[Good Friday]] on a Friday between March 20 and April 23, [[Easter]] on a Sunday between March 22 and April 25, [[Carnation Revolution#Legacy#Freedom Day|Freedom Day]] on April 25, [[International Workers' Day]] on May 1, [[Feast of Corpus Christi]] on a Thursday between May 21 and June 24, [[Portugal Day]] on June 10, [[Assumption Day]] on August 15, [[5 October 1910 revolution|Implementation of the Republic Day]] on October 5, [[All Saints' Day]] on November 1, {{ill|Restoration of the Independence (Portugal)|pt|Restauração da Independência|lt=Restoration of the Independence Day}} on December 1, [[Feast of the Immaculate Conception]] on December 8, and [[Christmas Day]] on December 25.<ref name="Labour Code IX.234" /> The regional holidays in Madeira are [[Madeira Day]] on July 1, and [[Boxing Day|1st Octave Day]] on December 26.<ref>{{cite act |author=Legislative Assembly of Madeira|author-link=Legislative Assembly of Madeira|trans-title=Regional Legislative Decree No. 17/2024/M|at=No. 206/2024, 1st Supplement, Series 1|location={{lang|pt-PT|Jornal Oficial da Região Autónoma da Madeira}} |url=https://joram.madeira.gov.pt/joram/1serie/Ano%20de%202024/ISerie-206-2024-12-16sup.pdf|date=16 December 2024|language=pt-PT|title=Decreto Legislativo Regional n.º 17/2024/M|access-date=3 May 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20250325021246/https://joram.madeira.gov.pt/joram/1serie/Ano%20de%202024/ISerie-206-2024-12-16sup.pdf|archive-date=25 March 2025|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite act |author=Legislative Assembly of Madeira|author-link=Legislative Assembly of Madeira|trans-title=Regional Legislative Decree No. 18/2002/M|at=No. 138/2002, Series 1|location={{lang|pt-PT|Jornal Oficial da Região Autónoma da Madeira}} |url=https://joram.madeira.gov.pt/joram/1serie/Ano%20de%202002/ISerie-138-2002-11-19.pdf|date=19 November 2002|language=pt-PT|title=Decreto Legislativo Regional n.º 18/2002/M|access-date=3 May 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240629030304/https://joram.madeira.gov.pt/joram/1serie/Ano%20de%202002/ISerie-138-2002-11-19.pdf|archive-date=29 June 2024|url-status=live}}</ref> The Azores celebrate [[Azores Day]] on a Monday between May 11 and June 14.<ref>{{cite act |author=Legislative Assembly of the Azores|author-link=Legislative Assembly of the Azores|trans-title=Regional Decree No. 13/80/A|at=No. 30/1980, Series 1|location={{lang|pt-PT|Jornal Oficial da Região Autónoma da Madeira}} |url=https://jo.azores.gov.pt/pdf/jornais/I-1980-030-S0.pdf|date=21 August 1980|language=pt-PT|title=Decreto Regional n.º 13/80/A |access-date=3 May 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260503215717/https://jo.azores.gov.pt/pdf/jornais/I-1980-030-S0.pdf|archive-date=3 May 2026|url-status=live}}</ref> Optional holidays in Portugal are the {{ill|Entrudo|pt|Entrudo|lt=Entrudo}} and one municipal holiday allowed per [[concelho]].<ref name="Labour Code IX.235">{{cite act|orig-section=Article 235 |author=Assembleia da República|trans-title=Law No. 7/2009 |at=No. 30/2009, Series 1|location={{lang|pt-PT|[[Diário da República]]}} |url=https://www.pgdlisboa.pt/leis/lei_mostra_articulado.php?artigo_id=1047A0235&nid=1047&tabela=leis&ficha=1&nversao=|date=12 February 2009|language=pt-PT|title=Lei n.º 7/2009|access-date=3 May 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260503221357/https://www.pgdlisboa.pt/leis/lei_mostra_articulado.php?artigo_id=1047A0235&nid=1047&tabela=leis&ficha=1&nversao=|archive-date=3 May 2026|url-status=live}}</ref>

=== Cuisine ===
{{Main|Portuguese cuisine|Portuguese wine}}

[[File:Funchal (Madeira, Portugal), Rua Dr. Fernão de Ornelas, Nata 7 - Fernão Ornelas -- 2025 -- 1205.jpg|thumb|{{lang|pt-PT|[[Pastel de nata|Pastéis de nata]]}}|alt=Photograph of a bakery display case filled with pastéis de nata, with a sign in front labelled “Pastel de Nata” and describing them as a low-sugar secret recipe in Portuguese and English.]]

Portuguese cuisine is influenced by both the [[Mediterranean diet|Mediterranean]] and [[Atlantic diet|Atlantic]] diets.<ref>{{cite journal|last1=Guiné |first1=Raquel P. F. |last2=Florença |first2=Sofia G. |last3=Amaral |first3=Ana Luisa |last4=Costa |first4=Cristina A. |publisher=De Gruyter|title=Reference dietary patterns in Portugal: Mediterranean diet vs Atlantic diet|journal=Open Agriculture |publication-date=8 January 2025 |volume=10|eissn=2391-9531 |article-number=20220406|issue=1|pages=1–2 |doi=10.1515/opag-2022-0406|doi-access=free|publication-place=Warsaw}}</ref> Seafood, ''[[brassicas]]'', potatoes, bread, dairy, and [[olive oil]] are traditional staples.<ref name="SEAD">{{cite journal |last1=Lorenzo |first1=Paula M |last2=Izquierdo |first2=Andrea G |last3=Rodriguez-Carnero |first3=Gemma |last4=Fernández-Pombo |first4=Antía |last5=Iglesias |first5=Alba |last6=Carreira |first6=Marcos C |last7=Tejera |first7=Cristina |last8=Bellido |first8=Diego |last9=Martinez-Olmos |first9=Miguel A |last10=Leis |first10=Rosaura |last11=Casanueva |first11=Felipe F |last12=Crujeiras |first12=Ana B |title=Epigenetic Effects of Healthy Foods and Lifestyle Habits from the Southern European Atlantic Diet Pattern: A Narrative Review |journal=Advances in Nutrition |date=September 2022 |volume=13 |issue=5 |pages=1725–1747 |doi=10.1093/advances/nmac038 |pmid=35421213 |pmc=9526853 }}</ref> {{lang|pt-PT|[[Bacalhau]]}} has such broad presence in Portugal that is considered a [[national dish]], along with {{lang|pt|[[pastel de nata]]}}.<ref>{{Cite conference |url=https://www.academia.edu/15680102|book-title=Heritages and Memories from the Sea|title=The fable of the cod and the promised sea: About Portuguese traditions of bacalhau|conference=1st International Conference of the UNESCO Chair in Intangible Heritage and Traditional Know-How: Linking Heritage|location=Évora|publisher=[[University of Évora]]|first= António José Marques da|last=Silva|access-date=13 April 2026|pages=132–133|publication-date=October 2015|date=14–16 January 2015|oclc=952343297|isbn=978-989-99442-0-6|editor-first1= Filipe Themudo|editor-last1=Barata|editor-first2=João Magalhães|editor-last2=Rocha|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260504003514/https://dspace.uevora.pt/rdpc/bitstream/10174/17186/1/Heritages%20and%20Memories%20from%20the%20Sea%20%281%29.pdf|archive-date=4 May 2026|via=Academia.edu|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{Cite book|chapter=Chapter 18: How to Internationalize a Traditional Portuguese-Style Food – Liability or Asset of Portugueseness?|doi=10.1108/S1745-886220170000012007|title=Distance in International Business: Concept, Cost and Value|volume=12|publisher= Emerald Publishing|pages=425–442|isbn=978-1-78743-718-0
|issn=1745-8862|oclc=1013889136|publication-place=Bingley|series=Progress in International Business Research|first1= Susana|last1=Costa e Silva|first2= Maria|last2=Elo|publication-date=30 November 2017|editor-first1=Alain|editor-last1=Verbeke|editor-first2= Jonas|editor-last2=Puck|editor-first3=Rob van|editor-last3=Tulder}}</ref> Traditional Portuguese sweets are known as [[conventual sweets]]. Large quantities of sugar and eggs are used.<ref>{{cite book|url=https://www.gastronomias.com/Livro%20de%20Do%E7aria%20Conventual.pdf|isbn=978-972-37045-0-1|title=Doçaria dos conventos de Portugal|language=pt-PT|trans-title=Portuguese convent sweets|publisher=Assírio & Alvim|year=1997|last1=Saramago|last2=Fialho|first1=Alfredo|first2=Manuel|pages=37–222|oclc=39724323|publication-place=Lisbon|series=Coração, cabeça e estômago|volume=1|access-date=4 May 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260428063339/https://www.gastronomias.com/Livro%20de%20Do%E7aria%20Conventual.pdf|archive-date=28 April 2026|url-status=live}}</ref>

Popular Portuguese beverages include its wines, a craft that was introduced in Portugal by the Romans, and of which are such notable examples as [[Port wine|Port]] and [[Madeira wine|Madeira]].<ref name="romanico">{{cite web |title=O vinho na antiguidade clássica - Alguns apontamentos sobre Lousada|url=http://www.rotadoromanico.com/SiteCollectionDocuments/Romanico_Mais%20Informacao/Revista%20OPPIDUM/O_vinho_na_antiguidade_classica_pp.69-85.pdf |access-date= May 24, 2017|publisher=Oppidum|language=pt|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180914165453/http://www.rotadoromanico.com/SiteCollectionDocuments/Romanico_Mais%20Informacao/Revista%20OPPIDUM/O_vinho_na_antiguidade_classica_pp.69-85.pdf |archive-date=September 14, 2018|url-status=dead}}</ref> [[Beer in Portugal|Beer]] has been brewed in Portugal beginning in [[Lusitania]].<ref>{{cite journal|doi=10.1017/S1062798724000346|doi-access=free|journal=European Review|publisher=Cambridge University Press|title=Wine and Portugal: A Brief History|publication-date=18 February 2025|volume=33|issue=1|url=https://www.cambridge.org/core/services/aop-cambridge-core/content/view/1D8A780317C586A218C446F31FBCE780/S1062798724000346a.pdf/wine-and-portugal-a-brief-history.pdf|first=Stefan K.|last=Estreicher|pages=38–129 |access-date=13 April 2026}}</ref> Tea has been produced on [[São Miguel Island]] since the 19th century.<ref>{{Cite thesis|title=Introdução da cultura do chá na ilha de São Miguel no século XIX (subsídios históricos)|year=2019|first=Mário Fernando de Oliveira|last=Moura|hdl=10400.3/5054|publisher=[[University of the Azores]]|publication-place=[[Ponta Delgada]]|access-date=13 April 2026|url=https://repositorio.uac.pt/bitstreams/bb999648-8244-484e-9354-ab3092ec14f9/download|hdl-access=free|type=Doctoral thesis}}</ref>

=== Sport ===
{{Main|Sport in Portugal}}

[[File:Cristiano Ronaldo Portugal.jpg|thumb|left|upright|[[Cristiano Ronaldo]] is widely considered one of the greatest football players of all time.]]

Portugal has contributed to the popularity and globalisation of sport through internationally recognised athletes such as [[Cristiano Ronaldo]], [[Ricardinho (futsal player, born 1985)|Ricardinho]], [[Naide Gomes]], and [[Carlos Lopes]], as well as through the [[List of sports clubs by membership|popularity]] of its three largest [[Big Three (Portugal)|football clubs]].<ref>{{cite book|page=2|chapter=Chapter 1: Sport in the Iberian Peninsula: An introduction|publication-date=3 November 2022|doi=10.4324/9781003197003-1|oclc=1344489817|title=Sport in the lberian peninsula: management, economics and policy|series=Routledge research in sport business and management|lccn=2022025248|isbn=9781003197003|editor-last1=García-Fernández|editor-first1=Jerónimo|editor-last2=Grimaldi-Puyana|editor-first2=Moisés|editor-last3=Bravo|editor-first3=Gonzalo A.|edition=1st|publisher=Routledge|publication-place=Abingdon|last1=García-Fernández|first1=Jerónimo|last2=Grimaldi-Puyana|first2=Moisés|last3=Bravo|first3=Gonzalo A.}}</ref><ref>{{cite book|page=36|chapter=Chapter 4: The sport systems in Spain and Portugal|publication-date=3 November 2022|doi=10.4324/9781003197003-4|oclc=1344489817|title=Sport in the lberian peninsula: management, economics and policy|series=Routledge research in sport business and management|lccn=2022025248|isbn=9781003197003|editor-last1=García-Fernández|editor-first1=Jerónimo|editor-last2=Grimaldi-Puyana|editor-first2=Moisés|editor-last3=Bravo|editor-first3=Gonzalo A.|edition=1st|publisher=Routledge|publication-place=Abingdon|last1=Carvalho|first1=Maria José|last2=García-Cirac|first2=María Josefa|last3=Sousa|first3=Marisa}}</ref> [[Portuguese football|Football]] is the most popular sport in Portugal.<ref>{{cite journal|issn=1466-0970|eissn=1743-9590|first=Pedro|last=Almeida|pages=75–88|volume=23|issue=1|title=Football, race and national identity in Portugal|doi=10.1080/14660970.2021.1920013|journal=Soccer & Society|publication-date=2 January 2022|publisher=Routledge|publication-place=Abingdon}}</ref> The [[Portugal men's national football team]] won the [[UEFA European Championship]] in [[UEFA Euro 2016|2016]] and the [[UEFA Nations League]] in [[2018–19 UEFA Nations League|2019]] and [[2024–25 UEFA Nations League|2025]].<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.uefa.com/newsfiles/EURO/2016/2017907_FR.pdf|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260511023357/https://www.uefa.com/newsfiles/EURO/2016/2017907_FR.pdf|url-status=live|archive-date=11 May 2026 |title=Full Time Report Final - Sunday 10 July 2016 Stade de France - Saint-Denis|author=UEFA|publisher=self-published |date=10 July 2016|access-date=11 May 2026}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.uefa.com/newsfiles/UNL/2019/2024422_FR.pdf|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260511015341/https://www.uefa.com/newsfiles/UNL/2019/2024422_FR.pdf|url-status=live|archive-date=11 May 2026 |title=Full Time Report Final - Sunday 9 June 2019 - Estádio do Dragão - Porto|author=UEFA|publisher=self-published |date=9 June 2019 |access-date=11 May 2026}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.uefa.com/newsfiles/UNL/2025/2044949_FR.pdf Portugal is among the world's leading [[Futsal in Portugal|futsal]] countries,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://inside.fifa.com/fifa-rankings|author=FIFA|publisher=self-published|access-date=11 May 2026|date=8 May 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260511052247/https://inside.fifa.com/fifa-rankings|archive-date=11 May 2026|url-status=live|title=FIFA Rankings}}</ref> with its [[Portugal national futsal team|men's national team]] having won the [[FIFA Futsal World Cup]] in [[2021 FIFA Futsal World Cup|2021]],<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.uefa.com/futsalworldcup/news/0257-0de805f9ebe1-fdf0b055945a-1000--2021-fifa-futsal-world-cup-portugal-beat-argentina-in-final/|title=2021 FIFA Futsal World Cup: Portugal beat Argentina in final|author=FIFA|publisher=self-published|date=30 September 2021|access-date=11 May 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211022183728/https://www.uefa.com/futsalworldcup/news/0257-0de805f9ebe1-fdf0b055945a-1000--2021-fifa-futsal-world-cup-portugal-beat-argentina-in-final/|archive-date=22 October 2021|url-status=live}}</ref> the [[UEFA Futsal Championship]] in [[UEFA Futsal Euro 2018|2018]] and [[UEFA Futsal Euro 2022|2022]],<ref>{{cite report|title=UEFA Futsal EURO 2018 tournament review|url=https://www.uefa.com/MultimediaFiles/Download/Publications/uefaorg/General/02/56/34/94/2563494_DOWNLOAD.pdf|page=23|author=UEFA|publisher=self-published|publication-date=22 June 2018|publication-place=Nyon|access-date=11 May 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180629130932/http://www.uefa.com/MultimediaFiles/Download/Publications/uefaorg/General/02/56/34/94/2563494_DOWNLOAD.pdf|archive-date=29 June 2018|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite report|title=UEFA Futsal EURO 2022 tournament review|url=https://indd.adobe.com/view/publication/963db25e-f04e-4891-9cf2-9d50b41c2385/nble/publication-web-resources/pdf/EURO_Futsal_2022_Tournament-Review_EN.pdf|page=27|author=UEFA|publisher=self-published|publication-date=2022|publication-place=Nyon|access-date=11 May 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20241106084233/https://indd.adobe.com/view/publication/963db25e-f04e-4891-9cf2-9d50b41c2385/nble/publication-web-resources/pdf/EURO_Futsal_2022_Tournament-Review_EN.pdf|archive-date=6 November 2024|url-status=live}}</ref> and the [[Futsal Finalissima]] in [[2022 Futsal Finalissima|2022]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.uefa.com/futsalfinalissima/match/2036154--spain-vs-portugal/|title=Spain-Portugal|author=UEFA|publisher=self-published|date=18 September 2022|access-date=11 May 2026|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20260511063133/https://www.uefa.com/futsalfinalissima/match/2036154--spain-vs-portugal/|archive-date=11 May 2026|url-status=live}}</ref> In {{ill|Sport of athletics in Portugal|pt|Atletismo em Portugal|lt=athletics}}, the country has set several [[List of Portuguese records in athletics|records]] and has earned more medals in this sport than in any other at both the [[Portugal at the Olympics|Olympic]] and [[Portugal at the Paralympics|Paralympic Games]].<ref>{{cite report|pages=54–95|url=https://fpaportalonline.blob.core.windows.net/portalfpa-public/2025/04/RAC_2024_VF.pdf|title=Relatório de Atividades e Contas Portugal|publication-date=1 November 2024|publisher=self-published|access-date=11 May 2026}}</ref><ref>{{cite [[jogo do pau]] and {{ill|Jogo da malha|pt|Jogo da malha|lt=jogo da malha}}.<ref>{{cite journal|doi=10.4000/tourisme.3019|publisher=Éditions touristiques européennes|journal=Mondes du destinations and have hosted motorsport events such as [[Portuguese Grand Prix|Formula One]] and [[Portuguese motorcycle Grand Prix|Grand Prix motorcycle racing]],<ref>{{cite
